The Sabab-Shart Distinction: The Multiplication Test
Analyzing the principle of sabab and shart with examples from fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that distinguishes sabab (cause) from shart (condition) using the test of multiplication of obligation and attribution.

Core Idea
A cause repeats with the obligation; a condition does not.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, it is crucial to distinguish between the cause (sabab) that necessitates a ruling and the condition (shart) that enables the cause to operate. This lesson introduces the key tests: attribution and multiplication. You will learn how to identify the cause by checking whether the obligation multiplies with the multiplicity of that element and whether the ruling is attributed to it in the primary text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Element
Look at the element in question (e.g., heads for zakat, time for Fitr, the House for Hajj). Determine if the ruling is directly attributed to it in the Quran or Sunnah.
Attribution is key: the obligation is linked to the cause, not the condition.
2
Apply the Multiplication Test
Check if the obligation increases when this element increases. For example, with more heads, zakat increases; with more time (days), zakat does not multiply.
If the obligation multiplies with the element, it is likely a cause.
3
Distinguish from Conditions
Conditions are necessary for the cause to operate but do not cause multiplication. They are attributed metaphorically, not directly.
Examples: time of Fitr, hadath for purification, istita'ah for Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبطل الثاني ؛ لاستحالة الوجوب على العبد والكافر والفقير، فعلم به أنه سبب، ولذلك يتضاعف الوجوب بتضاعف الرؤوس. وأما وقت الفطر فشرطه حتى لا يعمل السبب إلا بهذا الشرط، وإنما نُسب إلى الفطر مجازاً، والنسبة تحتمل الاستعارة، فأما تضاعف الوجوب فلا يحتمل الاستعارة. وبيان قولنا : إن الإضافة تحتمل الاستعارة: ظاهر؛ لأن الشيء يضاف إلى الشرط مجازاً، فأما تَضَاعُفُ الوجوب، فلا يحتمل الاستعارة؛ لأن الوجوب إنما يكون بسبب أو علة، لا يكون بغير ذلك، وهذا لا تتصور فيه الاستعارة، وكذلك وصف المؤنة يُرجّح الرأس في كونه سبباً، وقد بينا معنى المؤنة منه في موضعه. وسبب وجوب حج البيت أنه يُنسب إليه، ولم يتكرر، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ ﴾ آل عمران / ۹۷ وأما الوقت : فهو شرط الأداء، بدلالة أنه لا يتكرر بتكرره، غير أن الأداء شرع متفرقاً منقسماً على أمكنة وأزمنة يشتمل عليها جملة وقت الحج، فلم يصح تغييرُ الترتيب كما لا يصح السجود قبل الركوع، فلذلك لم يجز طواف الزيارة قبل يوم النحر، والوقوف قبل يوم عرفة. وأما الاستطاعة بالمال : فشرط، لا سبب ؛ لما ذكرنا إنه لا يُنسب إليه، ولا يتكرر بتكرره، ويصح الأداء دونه من الفقراء. ألا يُرى أنه عبادة بدنية، فلا يصلح المال سبباً لها، ولكنها عبادة هجرة وزيارة، فكان البيت سبباً لها. وسبب وجوب العُشر : الأرض النامية بحقيقة الخارج؛ لأن العشر يُنسب إلى الأرض، وفي العُشر معنى مؤنة الأرض؛ لأنها أصل، وفيه معنى العبادة؛ لأن الخارج للسبب وصف، وصار السبب بتجدد وصفه متجدداً في التقدير، فلم يجز التعجيل قبل الخارج؛ لأن الخارج بمعنى السبب لوصف العبادة، فلو صح التعجيل لخلص معنى المؤنة، فلما صارت به الأرض ناميةً : أشبه تعجيل زكاة السائمة، والإبل العلوفة، ثم أسامها. وكذلك سبب الخراج، إلا أن النماء معتبر في الخراج تقديراً، لا تحقيقاً بالتمكن به من الزراعة فصار مؤنةً باعتبار الأصل، وعقوبة باعتبار الوصف؛ لأن الزراعة عمارة للدنيا، وإعراض عن الجهاد، فكان سبباً لضرب من المذلة، ولذلك لم يجتمعا عندنا. وسبب وجوب الطهارة الصلاة؛ لأنها تُنسب إليها، وتقوم بها، وهي شرطها، فتعلقت بها، حتى لم تجب قصداً، لكن عند إرادة الصلاة، والحدث شرطه بمنزلة سائر شروط الصلاة، ومن المحال أن يُجعل الحدث سبباً ، ألا يُرى أنه إزالة له وتبديل له، فلا يصلح سبباً له. وأما سبب الحدود والعقوبات فما تُنسب إليه من قتل، وزناً، وسرقة. وسبب الكفارات : ما نُسبت إليه من أمر دائر بين حظر وإباحة، مثل الفطر، وقتل الخاطئ، وقتل الصيد، واليمين، ونحوها. وقتل العمد واليمين الغموس وما أشبه ذلك: لا يصلح سبباً
And the second is invalid because it is impossible for obligation to be upon the slave, the disbeliever, and the poor. Thus it is known by this that it (the head) is a cause, and therefore the obligation multiplies with multiplicity of heads. As for the time of Fitr, it is a condition so that the cause does not operate except with this condition. It is attributed to Fitr metaphorically, and attribution admits of metaphor. As for the multiplication of the obligation, it does not admit of metaphor. Explanation of our statement: 'Attribution admits of metaphor' is apparent because a thing is attributed to its condition metaphorically. As for the multiplication of the obligation, it does not admit of metaphor because obligation occurs only by a cause or an effective cause (illah), not otherwise, and metaphor is unimaginable in this. Likewise, the description of maintenance (mu'nah) gives preponderance to the head as being a cause, and we have explained the meaning of mu'nah in its place. The cause for the obligation of Hajj to the House is that it is attributed to it, and it does not repeat. Allah Most High said: 'And for Allah upon the people is the pilgrimage to the House' (Aal Imran 97). As for the time, it is a condition for performance, indicated by the fact that it does not repeat with its repetition. However, the performance is legislated in a distributed manner, divided over places and times that are included in the totality of the time of Hajj, so changing the order is not valid, just as prostration before bowing is not valid. Therefore, the visitation circumambulation (tawaf al-ziyarah) is not permissible before the Day of Nahr, nor standing (wuquf) before the Day of Arafah. As for capability (istita'ah) with wealth, it is a condition, not a cause, because as we mentioned, it is not attributed to it (the obligation) and does not repeat with its repetition, and performance is valid without it from the poor. Do you not see that it is a physical act of worship, so wealth cannot be a cause for it, but it is an act of emigration and visitation, so the House is the cause for it. The cause for the obligation of 'ushr (tithe) is the productive land by the reality of the produce, because the tithe is attributed to the land. In 'ushr, there is the meaning of maintenance (mu'nah) of the land because it is the original, and in it there is the meaning of worship because the produce is a description for the cause, and the cause becomes, by the renewal of its description, renewed in estimation. Therefore, acceleration (ta'jil) is not permissible before the produce, because the produce is in the sense of the cause due to the description of worship. If acceleration were valid, the meaning of maintenance would be pure. When the land becomes productive by it, it resembles the acceleration of zakat on grazing livestock and fed camels, then their turning loose. Likewise, the cause of kharaj (land tax) is similar, except that growth is considered in kharaj in estimation, not in actuality, by the ability to cultivate. Thus it becomes a maintenance due to the original, and a penalty due to the description, because cultivation is for the prosperity of the world and turning away from jihad, so it becomes a cause for a type of humiliation. Therefore, they (ushr and kharaj) do not combine according to us. The cause for the obligation of purification (taharah) is prayer because it is attributed to it and subsists by it, and it is a condition for it, so it is attached to it, such that it is not obligatory in itself, but at the time of intending prayer. The hadath (state of impurity) is a condition like the other conditions of prayer. It is impossible to make hadath a cause; do you not see that it removes it and changes it, so it cannot be a cause for it. As for the cause of fixed penalties (hudud) and punishments, they are attributed to killing, adultery, and theft. The cause of expiations (kaffarat) is that which they are attributed to, from matters oscillating between prohibition and permission, such as breaking fast, accidental killing, killing game, oaths, and the like. Intentional killing, the false oath (yamin ghamus), and similar, cannot be a cause.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's Kanz al-Wusul presents a foundational usul rule: distinguishing the legal cause (sabab) from the condition (shart). The author starts by arguing that the cause of an obligation is what it is attributed to and repeats with repetition (e.g., heads in zakat). Conditions, like the time of Fitr for zakat, are not causes; attribution to them is metaphorical. He then applies this to various acts. For Hajj, the cause is the House itself, as per the Quranic verse. The time and physical ability are conditions. For 'ushr, the land is the cause; the produce is a description that renews the cause, so acceleration is invalid. Kharaj is similar but carries a penal element, so 'ushr and kharaj do not combine. For purification, the cause is prayer, not hadath. For hudud and kaffarat, the cause is the attributed act, with exceptions like intentional killing and false oaths. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each example to illustrate the principle.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): That which the obligation is attributed to and repeats with repetition, making the obligation necessary.
شرط (shart): A condition that enables the cause to produce its effect but does not cause the ruling itself and does not repeat with repetition.
مؤنة (mu'nah): Maintenance or support; a quality that indicates the cause, as in the head being a cause due to the mu'nah of zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary indicator that an element is a cause (sabab) rather than a condition (shart)?
A) The obligation is attributed to it and multiplies with its multiplicity.
B) The obligation cannot be performed without it.
C) It is mentioned in the Quran.
D) It is a physical object.

Key Takeaway
To identify a cause, look for direct attribution and multiplication of obligation; conditions enable but do not cause multiplication.

Case Studies: Cause vs Condition in Hajj, Zakat, 'Ushr, Kharaj, Purification, and Penalties
Analyzing the principle of sabab and shart with examples from fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the cause (sabab) and condition (shart) in specific fiqh examples from the Hanafi tradition, including Hajj, zakat, 'ushr, kharaj, purification, hudud, and kaffarat.

Core Idea
In each act, the cause is what the obligation is attributed to and multiplies; conditions are external prerequisites.

Al-Bazdawi provides a series of concrete examples to illustrate how the sabab-shart distinction operates in different areas of fiqh. By working through each case, you will solidify your ability to apply the multiplication and attribution tests. This lesson walks through the examples of Hajj, zakat, 'ushr, kharaj, purification (taharah), hudud, and kaffarat, identifying the cause and condition for each.

Guided Path
1
Read Each Example
For each example (zakat, Hajj, 'ushr, etc.), read the author's statement and identify which element is argued to be the cause and which is the condition.
The author often uses phrases like 'attributed to' and 'multiplies with' to signal the cause.
2
Apply the Two Tests
For each identified element, ask: (1) Is the obligation directly attributed to this element? (2) Does the obligation multiply with its multiplicity? If yes, it is a cause. If no, it is a condition.
Note the exceptions: e.g., intentional killing fails because it does not oscillate between permission and prohibition.
3
Understand the Reasoning
The author provides reasons for each assignment. For example, time is a condition because it does not repeat; land is a cause for 'ushr because the tithe is attributed to it.
These reasons are based on the primary texts and the principle of mu'nah (maintenance).

Source Text

يكون بسبب أو علة، لا يكون بغير ذلك، وهذا لا تتصور فيه الاستعارة، وكذلك وصف المؤنة يُرجّح الرأس في كونه سبباً، وقد بينا معنى المؤنة منه في موضعه. وسبب وجوب حج البيت أنه يُنسب إليه، ولم يتكرر، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ ﴾ آل عمران / ۹۷ وأما الوقت : فهو شرط الأداء، بدلالة أنه لا يتكرر بتكرره، غير أن الأداء شرع متفرقاً منقسماً على أمكنة وأزمنة يشتمل عليها جملة وقت الحج، فلم يصح تغييرُ الترتيب كما لا يصح السجود قبل الركوع، فلذلك لم يجز طواف الزيارة قبل يوم النحر، والوقوف قبل يوم عرفة. وأما الاستطاعة بالمال : فشرط، لا سبب ؛ لما ذكرنا إنه لا يُنسب إليه، ولا يتكرر بتكرره، ويصح الأداء دونه من الفقراء. ألا يُرى أنه عبادة بدنية، فلا يصلح المال سبباً لها، ولكنها عبادة هجرة وزيارة، فكان البيت سبباً لها. وسبب وجوب العُشر : الأرض النامية بحقيقة الخارج؛ لأن العشر يُنسب إلى الأرض، وفي العُشر معنى مؤنة الأرض؛ لأنها أصل، وفيه معنى العبادة؛ لأن الخارج للسبب وصف، وصار السبب بتجدد وصفه متجدداً في التقدير، فلم يجز التعجيل قبل الخارج؛ لأن الخارج بمعنى السبب لوصف العبادة، فلو صح التعجيل لخلص معنى المؤنة، فلما صارت به الأرض ناميةً : أشبه تعجيل زكاة السائمة، والإبل العلوفة، ثم أسامها. وكذلك سبب الخراج، إلا أن النماء معتبر في الخراج تقديراً، لا تحقيقاً بالتمكن به من الزراعة فصار مؤنةً باعتبار الأصل، وعقوبة باعتبار الوصف؛ لأن الزراعة عمارة للدنيا، وإعراض عن الجهاد، فكان سبباً لضرب من المذلة، ولذلك لم يجتمعا عندنا. وسبب وجوب الطهارة الصلاة؛ لأنها تُنسب إليها، وتقوم بها، وهي شرطها، فتعلقت بها، حتى لم تجب قصداً، لكن عند إرادة الصلاة، والحدث شرطه بمنزلة سائر شروط الصلاة، ومن المحال أن يُجعل الحدث سبباً ، ألا يُرى أنه إزالة له وتبديل له، فلا يصلح سبباً له. وأما سبب الحدود والعقوبات فما تُنسب إليه من قتل، وزناً، وسرقة. وسبب الكفارات : ما نُسبت إليه من أمر دائر بين حظر وإباحة، مثل الفطر، وقتل الخاطئ، وقتل الصيد، واليمين، ونحوها. وقتل العمد واليمين الغموس وما أشبه ذلك: لا يصلح سبباً
And the second is invalid because it is impossible for obligation to be upon the slave, the disbeliever, and the poor. Thus it is known by this that it (the head) is a cause, and therefore the obligation multiplies with multiplicity of heads. As for the time of Fitr, it is a condition so that the cause does not operate except with this condition. It is attributed to Fitr metaphorically, and attribution admits of metaphor. As for the multiplication of the obligation, it does not admit of metaphor. Explanation of our statement: 'Attribution admits of metaphor' is apparent because a thing is attributed to its condition metaphorically. As for the multiplication of the obligation, it does not admit of metaphor because obligation occurs only by a cause or an effective cause (illah), not otherwise, and metaphor is unimaginable in this. Likewise, the description of maintenance (mu'nah) gives preponderance to the head as being a cause, and we have explained the meaning of mu'nah in its place. The cause for the obligation of Hajj to the House is that it is attributed to it, and it does not repeat. Allah Most High said: 'And for Allah upon the people is the pilgrimage to the House' (Aal Imran 97). As for the time, it is a condition for performance, indicated by the fact that it does not repeat with its repetition. However, the performance is legislated in a distributed manner, divided over places and times that are included in the totality of the time of Hajj, so changing the order is not valid, just as prostration before bowing is not valid. Therefore, the visitation circumambulation (tawaf al-ziyarah) is not permissible before the Day of Nahr, nor standing (wuquf) before the Day of Arafah. As for capability (istita'ah) with wealth, it is a condition, not a cause, because as we mentioned, it is not attributed to it (the obligation) and does not repeat with its repetition, and performance is valid without it from the poor. Do you not see that it is a physical act of worship, so wealth cannot be a cause for it, but it is an act of emigration and visitation, so the House is the cause for it. The cause for the obligation of 'ushr (tithe) is the productive land by the reality of the produce, because the tithe is attributed to the land. In 'ushr, there is the meaning of maintenance (mu'nah) of the land because it is the original, and in it there is the meaning of worship because the produce is a description for the cause, and the cause becomes, by the renewal of its description, renewed in estimation. Therefore, acceleration (ta'jil) is not permissible before the produce, because the produce is in the sense of the cause due to the description of worship. If acceleration were valid, the meaning of maintenance would be pure. When the land becomes productive by it, it resembles the acceleration of zakat on grazing livestock and fed camels, then their turning loose. Likewise, the cause of kharaj (land tax) is similar, except that growth is considered in kharaj in estimation, not in actuality, by the ability to cultivate. Thus it becomes a maintenance due to the original, and a penalty due to the description, because cultivation is for the prosperity of the world and turning away from jihad, so it becomes a cause for a type of humiliation. Therefore, they (ushr and kharaj) do not combine according to us. The cause for the obligation of purification (taharah) is prayer because it is attributed to it and subsists by it, and it is a condition for it, so it is attached to it, such that it is not obligatory in itself, but at the time of intending prayer. The hadath (state of impurity) is a condition like the other conditions of prayer. It is impossible to make hadath a cause; do you not see that it removes it and changes it, so it cannot be a cause for it. As for the cause of fixed penalties (hudud) and punishments, they are attributed to killing, adultery, and theft. The cause of expiations (kaffarat) is that which they are attributed to, from matters oscillating between prohibition and permission, such as breaking fast, accidental killing, killing game, oaths, and the like. Intentional killing, the false oath (yamin ghamus), and similar, cannot be a cause.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's Kanz al-Wusul presents a foundational usul rule: distinguishing the legal cause (sabab) from the condition (shart). The author starts by arguing that the cause of an obligation is what it is attributed to and repeats with repetition (e.g., heads in zakat). Conditions, like the time of Fitr for zakat, are not causes; attribution to them is metaphorical. He then applies this to various acts. For Hajj, the cause is the House itself, as per the Quranic verse. The time and physical ability are conditions. For 'ushr, the land is the cause; the produce is a description that renews the cause, so acceleration is invalid. Kharaj is similar but carries a penal element, so 'ushr and kharaj do not combine. For purification, the cause is prayer, not hadath. For hudud and kaffarat, the cause is the attributed act, with exceptions like intentional killing and false oaths. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each example to illustrate the principle.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): That which the obligation is attributed to and repeats with repetition, making the obligation necessary.
شرط (shart): A condition that enables the cause to produce its effect but does not cause the ruling itself and does not repeat with repetition.
مؤنة (mu'nah): Maintenance or support; a quality that indicates the cause, as in the head being a cause due to the mu'nah of zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that intentional killing (qatl 'amd) cannot be a cause for kaffarah?
A) Because it is a sin.
B) Because it does not oscillate between prohibition and permission.
C) Because it is attributed to the killer.
D) Because it multiplies with repetition.

Key Takeaway
The cause for kaffarah is an act that oscillates between prohibition and permission; purely sinful acts cannot be causes.

Faith (Iman) as a Condition for Narrator Reliability
Defining iman/islam and its two types for narrator reliability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a candidate narrator's faith as sufficient (zahir or thabit bil-bayan) for accepting his reports according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
General assent to Allah suffices for narrator reliability; detailed theological explanation is not required.

This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi addresses a critical question in hadith criticism: what level of faith (iman) is required for a narrator to be considered reliable? The author distinguishes between two types of iman: the apparent faith established by upbringing among Muslims, and the faith established by personal declaration. The key point is that demanding a detailed description of Allah's attributes is an unnecessary hardship; general assent (tasdiq) and verbal acknowledgment (iqrar) are sufficient.

Guided Path
1
Define the term iman/islam
Identify the legal definition given in the passage: tasdiq (assent) and iqrar (acknowledgment) of Allah with His attributes and acceptance of His laws.
Note that actions are not part of iman in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the two types of iman
Distinguish between iman zahir (apparent faith, established by being raised among Muslims) and iman thabit bil-bayan (faith established by one's own declaration and description of Allah).
These are the two ways a narrator's iman can be known.
3
Recognize the minimal condition
Understand that the second type (thabit bil-bayan) is a perfection that is not required as a condition because people's knowledge varies. The essential condition is that the narrator's assent and acknowledgment are established in general terms.
The passage explicitly says 'this is a perfection that is difficult to condition'.
4
Apply to narrator verification
See how this condition is practically assessed: it is sufficient to ask a generic question like 'Is he like that?' or to check that the narrator is known to be Muslim by upbringing or declaration.
This prevents hardship in evaluating narrators.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الإيمان والإسلام فإن تفسيره : التصديق والإقرار بالله سبحانه وتعالى كما هو بصفاته وأسمائه، وقبول شرائعه وأحكامه. وهو نوعان: ظاهر : بنشوئه بين المسلمين، وثبوتِ حكم الإسلام تبعاً لغيره من الوالدين. وثابت بالبيان بأن يصف الله تعالى كما هو، إلا أن هذا كمال يتعذر شرطه ؛ لأن معرفة الخلق بأوصافه على التفسير متفاوتة، وإنما شرط الكمال بما لا حرج فيه، وهو أن يثبت التصديق والإقرار بما قلنا إجمالاً وإن عجز عن بيانه وتفسيره. ولهذا قلنا : إن الواجب أن يُستوصَفَ المؤمن، فيقال : أهو كذا ؟
And as for faith (iman) and submission (islam): their interpretation is assent (tasdiq) and acknowledgment (iqrar) to Allah, the Exalted, as He is with His attributes and names, and acceptance of His laws and judgments. And it is of two types: apparent: by his upbringing among Muslims and the establishment of the ruling of Islam following others from the parents. And established by explanation (bayan) by his describing Allah as He is, except that this is a perfection that is difficult to condition; because the knowledge of creation of His attributes by interpretation varies, and the perfection is conditioned by that which does not involve hardship, and that is that the assent and acknowledgment are established for what we have said in general, even if he is incapable of explaining it and interpreting it. And for this reason we said: It is obligatory that the believer be asked about his faith, such that it is said: Is he like this?
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage defines the condition of iman and islam for accepting reports. The author states that iman/islam consist of tasdiq (assent) and iqrar (acknowledgment) of Allah with His attributes and names, and acceptance of His laws. These two types of faith are relevant for a narrator. First is 'zahir': faith established by being born and raised among Muslims, with the ruling of Islam applying by birth. Second is 'thabit bil-bayan': faith established by a person's own declaration and description of Allah as He is. However, the latter perfection is not required as a condition because people's knowledge varies. The essential condition is that the person's assent and acknowledgment are established in general terms, even if they cannot elaborate. Therefore, when examining a narrator's faith, it is sufficient to ask generically (e.g., 'Is he like that?') rather than demanding detailed theological exposition.

Key Terms
الإيمان (al-iman): Assent (tasdiq) and acknowledgment (iqrar) of Allah, His attributes, and His laws.
التصديق (al-tasdiq): Inner assent and belief in the heart regarding Allah and His teachings.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Verbal acknowledgment or declaration of faith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which type of iman is established by a person's own declaration and description of Allah?
A) Iman zahir (apparent faith)
B) Iman thabit bil-bayan (established by explanation)
C) Iman al-Islam (Islamic faith)
D) Iman al-tasdiq (faith of assent)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a narrator's faith is established by general assent and acknowledgment; detailed theological explanation is not required for accepting his reports.

Acceptance of Mere Affirmation of Faith and the Requirement of Description
Discussion on Prophet's practice of accepting general affirmation without detailed description.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that an absolute (mutlaq) declaration of faith suffices for belief, and distinguish when a failure to describe faith indicates its absence.

Core Idea
A general 'yes' to the shahada makes one a complete believer; detailed description is not required.

In matters of faith, the Hanafi school holds that a simple, unqualified affirmation of belief is enough to be considered a Muslim. This lesson explores the prophetic practice and the legal principle of mutlaq (absolute) as applied to faith, showing that the Quran and Sunnah support this position. We will also examine an exceptional case where failure to describe faith leads to a different ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Read the opening sentence: 'If he says: Yes, then the perfection of his Islam becomes apparent.' This is the core ruling—a mere affirmative response makes one a complete Muslim.
2
Trace the prophetic practice
The author cites the Prophet's habit of asking for a general description (istiswaaf) without demanding details. This shows that the absolute (mutlaq) covers the complete meaning.
The word مطلق (mutlaq) is a key usul term here.
3
Examine the Quranic dalil
Verse 60:10 commands examining believing women. The Prophet's examination was general, proving that absolute affirmation is sufficient.
The thubut of the Quran is qat'i, but its dalala is zanni in this context.
4
Apply the hadith evidence
Two hadiths are given: (1) regular congregation attendance, (2) praying our prayer, facing our qibla, eating our meat. These are signs of faith, not conditions. The mutlaq affirmation is still primary.
The hadiths support that observable signs confirm faith, but absence of signs does not negate a general declaration.
5
Analyze the exception
Imam Muhammad's ruling: a girl raised by Muslim parents who cannot describe Islam upon maturity is separated from her husband. This shows that when someone is specifically asked for description (istiswaaf) and fails, they are not a believer.
This is a fiqh application of the usul rule: the mutlaq is operative unless evidence of ignorance appears.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا قال: نعم: فقد ظهر كمال إسلامه. ألا يُرى أن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام استوصف فيما يُروى عنه عن ذكر الجُمَل دون التفسير، وكان ذلك دأبه صلى الله عليه وسلم. والمطلق من :هذا ما يقع على الكامل أيضاً، بذلك أمرنا بالكتاب والسنة. قال الله تعالى: ﴿ يَتَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا إِذَا جَاءَ كُمُ الْمُؤْمِنَتُ مُهَاجِرَاتِ فَامْتَحِنُوهُنَّ اللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِإِيمَتِهِنَّ الممتحنة / ١٠ . وكان النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام يمتحن الأعراب بعد دعوى الإيمان. إلا أن تظهر أماراتُه فيجب التسليم له كما قال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام : «إذا رأيتم الرجل يعتاد الجماعة فاشهدوا له بالإيمان». وقال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام: مَن صلى صلاتنا، واستقبل قبلتنا وأكَلَ ذبيحتنا : فاشهدوا له بالإيمان). فأما مَن استوصف، فجَهِلَ : فليس بمؤمن، كذا قال محمد رحمه الله في الجامع الكبير في الصغيرة بين أبوين مسلمين إذا لم تصف الإسلام حتى أدركت، فلم تصفه : أنها تبين من زوجها.
If he says: 'Yes', then the perfection of his Islam becomes apparent. Do you not see that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to ask for a description (istawsafa) in what is narrated about him mentioning the general statements without explanation, and that was his practice (peace be upon him). And the absolute (al-mutlaq) from this is what applies to the complete as well. We are commanded by the Book and the Sunnah to that. Allah Almighty said: 'O you who believe, when believing women come to you as emigrants, examine them. Allah knows best about their faith.' (Al-Mumtahanah: 10). And the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to examine the Bedouins after their claim of faith. Unless its signs appear, then submission is obligatory for him, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'If you see a man regularly attending the congregation, then testify for him with faith.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever prays our prayer, faces our Qibla, and eats our slaughtered meat, then testify for him with faith.' As for the one who is asked for a description and is ignorant, then he is not a believer. Thus said Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) in Al-Jami' al-Kabir concerning a minor girl between two Muslim parents: if she does not describe Islam until she reaches maturity, and she does not describe it, that she becomes separated from her husband.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage presents a usul rule about the acceptance of a general affirmation of faith. The author begins by stating that if a person simply says 'yes' to the shahada, their Islam is complete. He then cites the Prophet's practice (sunnah) of asking for a description (istiswaaf) in general terms without demanding details, which shows that absolute statements (mutlaq) cover the complete meaning. The Quranic verse (60:10) commands examination of believing women, and the Prophet's practice was to examine Bedouins with general questions about faith. The hadiths provide signs of faith: regular attendance at congregation and performing the prayer, facing the qibla, and eating halal meat. The passage then distinguishes: if someone is asked for a description and fails, they are not a believer, as exemplified by Imam Muhammad's ruling in al-Jami' al-Kabir: a girl raised by Muslim parents who cannot describe Islam upon maturity is separated from her husband, implying her apostasy or non-belief. The key point is that general acceptance suffices for faith; detailed knowledge is not a condition for belief but may indicate its absence when one cannot articulate it.

Key Terms
المطلق (al-mutlaq): In this context, 'absolute' refers to a general statement that covers the complete meaning without need for detail.
الاستوصاف (al-istiswaaf): The act of asking someone to describe their faith or belief.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) He asked him if he testifies to the shahada, and upon saying yes, he accepted him.
C) He sent him to a teacher to learn Islam.
D) He examined him with a written test.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, an absolute (mutlaq) declaration of faith suffices for belief; detailed description is not required unless specific circumstances indicate ignorance.

Acceptability of Narrators: Blind, Flogged for Slander, Women, and Slaves
Establishing that blind, flogged for slander, women, and slaves are acceptable narrators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule regarding the acceptance of narrators from these categories and explain why riwayah differs from shahadah.

Core Idea
Narration (riwayah) does not require wilayah; the hearer's obligation stems from his own duty to obey Allah.

This passage from Al-Bazdawi's Kanz al-Wusul clarifies an important usul principle: the conditions for accepting a narrator of religious knowledge are different from those for accepting a witness in legal cases. You will learn why the Hanafi school accepts reports from the blind, those flogged for slander, women, and slaves, despite their limitations as witnesses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
List the four types of narrators the passage declares acceptable: blind, flogged for slander, women, and slaves. Note that each faces a disability in shahadah but not in riwayah.
These are explicitly mentioned: الأعمى، المحدود في القذف، المرأة، العبد.
2
Recognize the distinction between riwayah and shahadah
Understand that shahadah (testimony) requires extra discernment (missing in blindness), complete transitive guardianship (wilayah muta'ddiyah, missing in slavery), and is deficient in women and those flogged for slander. Riwayah does not have these requirements.
The passage says: بخلاف الشهادات في حقوق الناس؛ لأنها تفتقر إلى تمييز زائد ينعدم بالعمى، وإلى ولاية كاملة متعدية تنعدم بالرق، وتقصر بالأنوثة، وبحد القذف.
3
Analyse the first reason riwayah is not wilayah
The obligation to accept a religious report (riwayah) arises from the hearer's own commitment to obey Allah and His Messenger, not from any authority of the narrator. Note the analogy to a judge: the judge is also obligated by the same commitment, not by the narrator's wilayah.
الوجه الأول: أن ما يلزم السامع من خبر المخبر بأمور الدين، فإنما يلزم بالتزامه طاعة الله تعالى ورسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم، كما يلزم القاضي... (the sentence is cut off).
4
Synthesize the overall rule
Combine the above: since riwayah does not fall under wilayah, the disabilities that affect shahadah (blindness, slavery, femininity, qadhf hadd) do not disqualify a narrator. The only requirement in riwayah is reliability (justice/adalah) and memory, which can be present in these categories.
The passage concludes: فأما هذا فليس من باب الولاية لوجهين... We are given one complete reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبتت هذه الجملة كان الأعمى، والمحدود في القذف، والمرأة، والعبد : من أهل الرواية، وكان خبرهم حجةً. بخلاف الشهادات في حقوق الناس؛ لأنها تفتقر إلى تمييز زائد ينعدم بالعمى، وإلى ولاية كاملة متعدية تنعدم بالرق، وتقصر بالأنوثة، وبحد القذف، على ما عُرف. فأما هذا فليس من باب الولاية ؛ لوجهين : أحدهما: أن ما يلزمُ السامعَ من خبر المخير بأمور الدين، فإنما يلزم بالتزامه طاعة الله تعالى ورسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم، كما يلزم القاضي
And when this statement is established, then the blind person, the one flogged for slander, the woman, and the slave are among the people of narration (riwayah), and their report is a proof. Unlike testimonies (shahadat) in the rights of people; because they require an extra discernment that is absent in blindness, and a complete transitive guardianship that is absent in slavery, and is deficient in femininity, and due to the hadd of slander, as is known. As for this [narration], it is not from the category of guardianship (wilayah) for two reasons: One of them is that what obligates the hearer from the report of the informer concerning matters of religion is only obligated by his commitment to obeying Allah Almighty and His Messenger (peace be upon him), just as it obligates the judge...
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for accepting narrators in religious matters (riwayah) versus witnesses in legal cases (shahadah). The author establishes that blind individuals, those who have been flogged for slander (al-mahdud fi al-qadhf), women, and slaves are all acceptable as narrators of religious reports (hadith, fatwa, etc.), and their reports are authoritative proofs (hujja). This is in contrast to the rules for legal testimony (shahadah) concerning the rights of people, which require: (1) full eyesight (discernment) – hence the blind are excluded; (2) complete transitive guardianship (wilayah) – hence slaves are excluded; (3) the quality of being a free male – women and those flogged for slander (whose testimony is rejected in hadd and qisas matters) are excluded. The passage then explains why narration (riwayah) does not fall under the category of guardianship (wilayah): the obligation to accept a religious report stems from the hearer's own duty to obey Allah and His Messenger, not from any authority of the narrator. The judge's obligation to accept testimony is similar but in a legal context. The second reason is cut off but likely concerns the nature of religious duty.

Key Terms
الرواية (al-riwayah): Narration or transmission of religious knowledge, especially hadith.
الشهادة (al-shahadah): Legal testimony in court, especially concerning rights of people (huquq al-nas).
الولاية (al-wilayah): Guardianship or authority, which is required for giving testimony but not for narrating religious knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a valid narrator (rawi) in religious matters according to the passage?
A) A blind person
B) A person flogged for slander
C) A woman
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts blind, flogged for slander, women, and slaves as narrators because riwayah is not a form of wilayah; the hearer's obligation stems from his own duty to obey Allah.

The Classification of Written Documents: 'Azima and Rukhsa
Classifies rulings on written documents into 'azima and rukhsa with imam opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi usul classification of acting upon written documents (khatt) into 'azima and rukhsa and identify the ikhtilaf among the three major imams.

Core Idea
Writing is credible only by 'azima if preserved; without preservation, rukhsa depends on context and imam.

This lesson from Usul al-Bazdawi presents a key usul topic: the evidentiary value of written documents. The three great Hanafi imams differ on when writing can be relied upon. Abu Hanifa holds a strict 'azima requiring preservation; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad grant concessions (rukhsa) in certain contexts. Understanding this classification is essential for evaluating written evidence in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three contexts
The passage discusses written documents in three areas: the judge's register (diwan al-qadi), hearing of hadith (sama' al-ahadith), and legal documents (sukuk).
2
Understand the 'azima position
Abu Hanifa holds that writing is only credible if it is preserved in one's own hand or with a trustee. This is the strict rule.
This is the 'azima; his narrations are few (qallat riwayatuhu).
3
Understand the rukhsa positions
Abu Yusuf permits acting on writing in diwan and hadith if preserved; for documents he does not. Muhammad permits in all three contexts, including documents by istihsan if the line is known and certain.
The rukhsa types are listed: (1) own hand secured, (2) known trustworthy hand secured, (3) known but not secured, (4) unknown.
4
Note the conditions for each type
Each type of writing has specific conditions regarding recognition and preservation. For example, unknown writing is invalid unless accompanied by sufficient context to prevent suspicion.
5
Apply the special cases
The passage gives two special cases: finding a father's or known person's line (one may report it as found, but no more) and unknown line (isolated = invalid, accompanied = valid).

وروي عن أبي يوسف رحمه الله : أنه يُعمل به في ديوان القاضي، وسماع الأحاديث، دون الصك. وروى ابن رستم عن محمد رحمه الله : أنه يُعمل بالخط في الكل. والعزيمةُ في هذا كله ما قاله أبو حنيفة رحمه الله، ولهذا قلت رواياتُه ، والرخصة فيما قالا فصارت الكتابة للحفظ : عزيمة، وبلا حفظ : رخصة. والعزيمة نوع واحد. والرخصة أنواع: ١ - ما يكون بخطه، موثقاً بيده، لا يحتمل تبديلاً. ۲ـ وكذلك ما يوجد بخط معروف لرجل ثقة موثق بيده. ٣- وما يكون بخط معروف، غير موثق بيده. ٤- وما يكون بخط مجهول. وذلك كله ثلاثة أنواع في الحديث والصكوك، وديوان القاضي. أما أبو يوسف فقد عمل به في ديوان القاضي إذا كان تحت يده؛ للأمن عن التزوير. وعمل به في الأحاديث إن كان بهذا الشرط. وأما إذا لم يكن في يده : لم يَحلَّ العمل به في الديوان؛ لأن التزوير في بابه غالب ؛ لِمَا يتصل بالمظالم وحقوق الناس. وأما في باب الحديث : فإن العمل به جائز إذا كان خطاً معروفاً لا يُخاف عليه التبديل في غالب العادة، ويُؤْمَنُ فيه الغلط؛ لأن التبديل فيه غير متعارف. والمحفوظ بيد الأمين : مثل المحفوظ بيده. وأما في الصكوك فلا يحل العمل به؛ لأنه تحت يد الخصم، إلا أن : يكون في يد الشاهد. وكذلك قول محمد رحمه الله، إلا في الصكوك: فإنه جوز العمل به وإن لم يكن في يده؛ استحساناً ؛ توسعةً على الناس إذا أحاط علماً بأنه خطه ، ولم يلحقه شكٍّ وشبهة، لأن الغلط في الخط نادر. بقي فصل، وهو ما يجده بخط أبيه، أو خط رجل معروف، كتاب معروف فيجوز أن يقول : وجدتُ بخط أبي، أو بخط فلان، لا يزيد على هذا. فأما الخط المجهول فعلى وجهين إما أن يكون مفرداً، وذلك باطل. وإما أن يكون مضموماً إلى جماعة لا يُتوهم التزوير في مثله، والنسبة تامة يقع بها التعريف فيكون كالمعروف، والله أعلم.
It is narrated from Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, that it (the writing) is acted upon in the register of the judge and in hearing hadith, but not in the document. And Ibn Rustam narrated from Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, that it is acted upon by the line in all. And the 'azima (strict ruling) in all this is what Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, said, and due to this his narrations are few, and the rukhsa (concession) is in what the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said. So the writing becomes for preservation: 'azima, and without preservation: rukhsa. And 'azima is one type. And rukhsa has types: 1. What is in his own handwriting, secured in his hand, not susceptible to alteration. 2. Likewise what is found in a known handwriting of a trustworthy man secured in his hand. 3. What is in a known handwriting, not secured in his hand. 4. What is in an unknown handwriting. And all that is three types in hadith, documents, and the judge's register. As for Abu Yusuf, he acted upon it in the judge's register if it was under his hand, due to security from forgery. And he acted upon it in hadith if it was with this condition. And if it was not in his hand, it is not permissible to act upon it in the register, because forgery in that chapter is prevalent due to its connection with grievances and people's rights. And as for the chapter of hadith, acting upon it is permissible if it is a known handwriting that is not feared to be altered in the usual case, and error is secured from it, because alteration in it is not customary. And what is preserved with a trustee is like that preserved with himself. And as for documents, it is not permissible to act upon it because it is under the hand of the opponent, unless it is in the hand of the witness. And likewise the statement of Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, except in documents: he permitted acting upon it even if it is not in his hand, by istihsan (juristic preference), as a concession for people, when he is certain that it is his line and no doubt or suspicion attaches to him, because error in writing is rare. A remaining section: regarding what one finds in the handwriting of his father, or the handwriting of a known man, a known book, then he may say: 'I found in my father's handwriting, or in the handwriting of so-and-so,' and he does not add to this. As for the unknown line, it is of two types: either it is isolated, and that is invalid; or it is accompanied by a group such that forgery is not suspected in the like of it, and the attribution is complete and identification occurs thereby, so it is like the known. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi classifies the ruling on acting upon written documents (khatt) in three contexts: the judge's register (diwan al-qadi), hearing of hadith (sama' al-ahadith), and legal documents (sukuk). The three major Hanafi imams differ. Abu Hanifa holds the 'azima (strict position): writing is only credible if it is preserved under the person's own hand or that of a trustee. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow concessions (rukhsa) in some cases. Four types of writing are listed: (1) one's own handwriting secured in hand, (2) a known trustworthy person's handwriting secured, (3) known but not secured, (4) unknown. These reduce to three categories when applied to the three contexts. Abu Yusuf permits acting on writing in the judge's register and hadith only if it is under the person's hand (to avoid forgery), but not in documents because they are with the opponent. Muhammad agrees except for documents, where he permits by istihsan if one is certain the writing is his, due to rarity of error in writing. The 'azima (strictness) is that writing for preservation is required; without preservation it becomes a rukhsa. The passage then discusses special cases: finding a father's or known person's handwriting – one may report it as such but no more. Unknown handwriting is invalid if isolated, but valid if accompanied by sufficient context to prevent suspicion of forgery. This is a key usul topic on the authority of written transmission.

Key Terms
عزيمة (ʿazīma): The strict, original ruling without concession; here, not acting on writing unless preserved.
رخصة (rukḥṣa): A concession that permits acting on writing under certain conditions (known hand, no fear of forgery).
خط (khaṭṭ): Handwriting or written document; its evidentiary value depends on preservation and recognition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is Abu Hanifa's position ('azima) regarding acting on writing?
A) It is always permissible regardless of preservation.
B) It is not permissible unless the writing is in one's own hand or with a trustee for preservation.
C) It is permissible only in hadith and documents.
D) It is permissible only in the judge's register.

Key Takeaway
The evidentiary value of written documents in Hanafi law depends on preservation and recognition, with 'azima requiring security and rukhsa allowing concessions in low-risk contexts.

Transmission of Texts: 'Azima and Rukhsa
Defines the two methods of transmitting texts: verbatim (azima) and paraphrasing (rukhsa).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'azima and rukhsa in transmission and state the condition for each.

Core Idea
Transmission of texts is either verbatim or paraphrased; each has its own rule of validity.

In Hanafi usul, the act of transmitting a heard text (tabligh) is not monolithic. This passage introduces two fundamental methods: the strict method of exact reproduction ('azima) and the concessional method of paraphrasing (rukhsa). Understanding this distinction is crucial for evaluating the authority of transmitted knowledge and for correctly applying rulings in narration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two divisions of tabligh
The passage states that the aspect of transmission is divided into two types. Recognize that these are 'azima and rukhsa.
2
Define 'azima
'Azima is defined as adhering to the heard wording (al-lafz al-masmū'). It requires verbatim reproduction.
This is the strict method, preferred for hadith.
3
Define rukhsa
Rukhsa is defined as transferring to a wording chosen by the transmitter (al-naql ilā lafẓ yakhtāruhu al-nāqil). It allows paraphrasing.
4
Note the condition for rukhsa
The passage implies that rukhsa is permissible only if the meaning is preserved. The condition is that the paraphrase must not distort the original meaning.
This condition ensures reliability despite flexibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
* وأما طَرَفُ التبليغ : فقسمان أيضاً: عزيمة، ورخصة: أما العزيمة فالتمسك باللفظ المسموع، وأما الرخصة: فالنقل إلى لفظ يختاره الناقل. وهذا باب شرط نقل المتون :
* And as for the aspect of transmission: it is also two types: 'azima and rukhsa. As for 'azima, it is adhering to the heard wording; and as for rukhsa, it is transferring to a wording chosen by the transmitter. And this is the chapter on the condition of transmitting texts:
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This brief passage introduces the topic of transmitting texts (tabligh). In Hanafi usul, transmission is the process of narrating hadith or legal texts. There are two methods: 'azima, which is the strict method of transmitting exactly as heard (word-for-word), and rukhsa, which allows the transmitter to paraphrase or choose alternative wording while preserving the meaning. The passage ends by indicating that what follows will detail the conditions required for permissible transmission of texts (shart naql al-mutun). This is foundational for understanding the reliability of transmitted knowledge.

Key Terms
تبليغ (tablīgh): The act of conveying a heard text to others; transmission.
لفظ مسموع (lafẓ masmūʿ): The exact wording as heard from the source.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the 'azima in transmission?
A) Transferring to a chosen wording.
B) Adhering to the heard wording exactly.
C) Adding commentary to the text.
D) Writing down the text without speaking.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, transmission may be verbatim ('azima) or paraphrased (rukhsa), with 'azima being the strict method.

Laws of Previous Prophets: The Hanafi Condition for Accepting Previous Revelations
Explains the third opinion and the Hanafi condition for accepting previous laws

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on shara'i' man qablana, identify the condition for their applicability, and apply the evidence used to support this view.

Core Idea
Previous prophets' laws bind us only if the Quran or Prophet confirms them without disapproval.

This lesson examines a key usul al-fiqh dispute: Are the laws of previous prophets (shara'i' man qablana) binding upon Muslims? The Hanafi school takes a middle path: these laws are not automatically binding nor completely abrogated. Instead, they are accepted only when the Quran or the Prophet narrates them without criticism. This careful approach reflects the Hanafi commitment to relying only on verified divine sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
Recognize that the ulema differed on whether laws of previous prophets (like the Torah and Gospel) are binding on Muslims. The Hanafi view is a third opinion.
The passage contrasts this with two other views: (1) original principle of specificity (khusus) and (2) unconditional abrogation.
2
Understand the evidence for the Hanafi view
Examine the Quranic verse on inheriting the Book (35:32) and the hadith where the Prophet rebukes Umar for consulting the Torah, stating that even Moses would have to follow him.
These show that the Prophet's law is universal and that previous revelations are not automatically authoritative.
3
Grasp the condition
The Hanafi position requires that a previous law be mentioned in the Quran or by the Prophet without any disapproval (inkar). This precaution is due to distortion and skepticism about the transmission from the People of the Book.
The passage calls this 'al-Mukhtar' (the chosen view).
4
See the application via qiyas
Imam Muhammad uses a previous law from the story of Thamud (water distribution) to derive the permissibility of muhaya'ah (taking turns) through qiyas, showing that confirmed previous laws can be used as evidence.
This demonstrates the practical Hanafi method: accept previous laws when verified, then use them analogically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مِنكُمْ شِرْعَةً وَمِنْهَا جَا المائدة / ٤٨ ؛ لأن الأصل في الشرائع الماضية: الخصوص ، ألا يُرى أنها كانت تحتمل الخصوص في المكان في رسولين بُعِثا في زمان واحد في مكانين، إلا أن يكون أحدهما تبعاً للآخر، كما قال في قصة إبراهيم عليه السلام : فَعَامَنَ لَهُ لُوطُ العنكبوت / ٢٦ . وكما كان هارون لموسى عليهما السلام، فكذلك في الزمان أيضاً، فصار الاختصاص في شرائعهم أصلاً، إلا بدليل. واحتج أهل المقالة الثالثة بأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان أصلاً في الشرائع، وكانت شريعته عامةً لكافة الناس، وكان وارثاً لما مضى من محاسن الشريعة ومكارم الأخلاق قال الله تبارك وتعالى: ﴿ ثُمَّ أَوْرَثْنَا الْكِتَبَ الَّذِينَ اصْطَفَيْنَا مِنْ عِبَادِنَا فاطر/٣٢. ورأى رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في يد عمر رضي الله عنه صحيفة، فقال: ما هي؟ فقال: التوراة فقال: أمتهوكون أنتم كما تهوكت اليهود والنصارى، والله لو كان أخي موسى حياً لما وَسِعَه إلا اتباعي ) . فصار الأصل الموافقة والألفة، لكن بالشرط الذي قلنا، ومعروف لا ينكر من فعل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم العمل بما وجده صحيحاً مما في الكتب، غير محرَّف، إلا أن ينزل وحي بخلافه. فثبت أن هذا هو الأصل، إلا أن التحريف من أهل الكتاب كان أمراً ظاهراً، وكذلك الحسد والعداوة والتلبيس كثير منهم، ووقعت الشبهة في نقلهم، فشَرَطنا في هذا أن يَقصَّ اللهُ تعالى، أو رسوله عليه الصلاة والسلام من غير إنكار ؛ احتياطاً في باب الدين. وهو المختار عندنا من الأقوال، بهذا الشرط الذي ذكرنا. قال الله تبارك وتعالى: ﴿مِلَّةَ أَبِيكُمْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ ) الحج / ٠٧٨ وقال: ﴿ قُلْ صَدَقَ اللَّهُ فَاتَّبِعُوا مِلَّةَ إِبْرَاهِيمَ حَنِيفًا آل عمران / ٩٥ . فعلى هذا الأصل يجري هذا الفصل. وقد احتج محمد رحمه الله في تصحيح المهايأة والقسمة بقول الله تعالى: ﴿وَنَبْتَهُمْ أَنَّ الْمَاءَ قِسْمَةٌ بَيْنَهُمْ كُلُّ شِرْبٍ مُحْتَضَرُ القمر / ٢٨. وقال: ﴿لَمَا شِرْبٌ وَلَكُمْ شِرْبُ يَوْمٍ تَعلُوم ) الشعراء / ١٥٥ . فاحتج محمد بهذا النص لإثبات الحكم به في غير المنصوص عليه بما هو نظيره، فثبت أن المذهب هو القول الذي اخترناه، والله أعلم.
"For you a law and a way" (Quran 5:48); because the principle in previous laws is specificity. Do you not see that they could bear specificity in place: two messengers sent in one time in two places, unless one is a follower of the other, as it said in the story of Abraham (peace be upon him): "And Lot believed in him" (Quran 29:26). And as Aaron was to Moses (peace be upon them). Similarly in time, so specificity became the principle in their laws, unless there is evidence. The proponents of the third opinion argued that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was the origin of laws, his law was general to all people, and he inherited what passed of good laws and noble ethics. Allah Almighty said: "Then We gave the Book as inheritance to those We chose from Our servants" (Quran 35:32). And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saw in the hand of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) a page and said: 'What is this?' He said: 'The Torah.' He said: 'Are you bewildered as the Jews and Christians were bewildered? By Allah, if my brother Moses were alive, he would have no option but to follow me.' So the principle became agreement and harmony, but with the condition we mentioned, and it is not unknown that the Prophet (peace be upon him) acted upon what he found to be correct in the books, unaffected, unless revelation came contrary to it. So it is established that this is the principle, except that distortion from the People of the Book was apparent, and likewise envy, enmity, and obfuscation were frequent among them, and doubt arose regarding their transmission. So we stipulated in this that Allah or His Messenger (peace be upon him) narrates it without disapproval, as a precaution in religious matters. This is the chosen view among us, with this condition we mentioned. Allah Almighty said: "The religion of your father Abraham" (Quran 22:78) and said: "Say, Allah has spoken truth, so follow the religion of Abraham, inclining toward truth" (Quran 3:95). On this principle this chapter proceeds. And Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) used as proof for validating muhaya'ah (alternating turns) and division the saying of Allah: "And inform them that the water is shared between them, each drink attended" (Quran 54:28) and said: "She has a drink and you have a drink on a known day" (Quran 26:155). So Muhammad used this text to establish the ruling in matters not explicitly mentioned by what is analogous to it. So it is established that the madhhab is the opinion we chose, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage is a discussion from Usul al-Fiqh on the topic of 'Shara'i' man qablana' (laws of those before us). The author argues that the preferred Hanafi view is that the laws of previous prophets are binding upon us only under a specific condition. The passage begins by referencing an opposing view that the original principle in previous laws was specificity (khusus) — meaning each community had its own specific law — and that this specificity was the default unless evidence indicated otherwise. Then it presents the third opinion (ahl al-muqala al-thalitha), which argues that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) was the foundation of all laws, his Shari'ah is universal, and he inherited the best of previous laws. This is supported by the Quranic verse about inheriting the Book and a hadith where the Prophet rebuked Umar for consulting the Torah, stating that even Moses would have to follow him. The author then concludes that the original principle is agreement (muwafaqah) and harmony (ulfah) with previous laws, but with an important condition: those laws are only accepted if they are narrated in the Quran or by the Prophet without any criticism or disapproval (inkar). This precaution is due to the distortion, envy, and doubt in the transmission from the People of the Book. The author also mentions that Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) used a text from the Quran about the people of Thamud (water distribution) to analogically derive the permissibility of muhaya'ah (alternating use) and qisma (division) in similar cases. This shows that the Hanafi school not only theoretically accepts previous laws when verified but also uses them as evidence in qiyas.

Key Terms
شرائع من قبلنا (shara'i' man qablana): The religious laws revealed to prophets before Muhammad (peace be upon him).
أصل (asl): The foundational principle or default ruling in a given matter.
مهايأة (muhaya'ah): An arrangement between two or more parties to take turns in using a shared property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view in this passage, when are the laws of previous prophets binding upon Muslims?
A) They are always binding unless abrogated by the Quran.
B) They are binding only if they are mentioned in the Quran or the Prophet's sunnah without any disapproval.
C) They are binding only if they are mentioned in the Torah or Gospel.
D) They are never binding because they were abrogated by the Shari'ah of Muhammad.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts laws of previous prophets only when confirmed in the Quran or authentic hadith without any disapproval, ensuring that only uncorrupted divine guidance is followed.

The Necessity of Intention in Wudu': A Usul Analysis of Taghayyur
Concluding argument on necessity of intention in wudu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the usul reasoning in the argument that wudu' without intention is invalid, and apply the concept of 'taghayyur' to distinguish between rational and unintelligible aspects of purification.

Core Idea
Intention in wudu' is required because the water's change (taghayyur) is not rationally comprehensible, so water only cleans naturally—but intention remains necessary.

This lesson examines a passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul that defends the necessity of intention in wudu'. The author argues against the notion that water's natural cleansing property makes intention irrelevant. By analyzing the concept of taghayyur (the change in water when used), we uncover a key usul principle: actions in ibadah must be grounded in understanding, and where understanding is absent, intention becomes critical.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and counterclaim
Read the passage and note that the author responds to an implicit claim: 'wudu' is valid without intention because water cleans by nature.' The author's counterclaim is that wudu' is not valid without intention.
The phrase 'wa lā yalzamunā anna al-wuḍūʾ ṣaḥḥa maʿa hādhā bi-ghayr al-niyyah' introduces the counterclaim.
2
Distinguish the two aspects of water
The author distinguishes between two aspects: (1) the change (taghayyur) in water when used for purification, which is established 'bi wajh lā yuʿqal' (in a way not rationally comprehensible), and (2) water's natural action, which is 'bi al-wajh alladhī yuʿqal' (in a rational way). Understand this distinction.
The 'taghayyur' refers to the water becoming musta'mal (used water); its mechanism is not fully understood rationally.
3
Trace the implication for intention
Since the taghayyur is unintelligible, water's role as a purifier is only in its natural aspect; therefore, intention from the person is needed to complete the act of worship and make it valid.
This implies that intention supplies the purpose that the unintelligible change cannot provide.
4
Reflect on the methodological exhortation
The author concludes by emphasizing that these are subtle boundaries that require reflection, fairness, and respect for the limits of Shari'ah and the Salaf. This reminds us that usul analysis requires humility and reverence.
The phrase 'wa hādhā ḥudūd lā yuhtadā li-darikihā' indicates the depth required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يلزمنا أن الوضوء صح مع هذا بغير النية؛ لأن التغيير ثبت محل العمل بوجه لا يُعقل، فبقي الماء عاملاً بطبعه من الوجه الذي يُعقل. وهذه حدود لا يُهتدى لدَرْكها إلا بالتأمل والإنصاف، وتعظيم حدود الشرع، وتوقير السلف رحمهم الله منَّةً من الله تعالى وفضلاً.
And it does not necessitate us that wudu' is correct with this without intention, because the change is established in the locus of action in a way that is not rationally comprehensible, so water remained acting by its nature in the way that is rational. And these are boundaries that cannot be perceived except through reflection and fairness, and magnifying the boundaries of the Shari'ah, and venerating the Salaf, may Allah have mercy on them, as a favor from Allah Most High and bounty.
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling regarding the validity of wudu' without intention. The author argues that it does not follow that wudu' is valid without intention, because the change (taghayyur) that occurs in water when used for purification is established in the locus of the action in an unintelligible manner. Thus, water continues to act by its natural property in a way that is rational. This implies that the need for intention remains. The passage concludes by emphasizing that these are subtle boundaries that can only be grasped through deep reflection, fairness, and respect for the limits set by the Shari'ah and the ways of the Salaf.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention, which is argued to be necessary for wudu' based on the unintelligible nature of water's change.
تغيير (taghayyur): The change in the property of water when used for purification, established in the locus of action in an unintelligible way.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is wudu' without intention invalid?
A) Because water becomes impure after use
B) Because the change (taghayyur) in water is not rationally comprehensible
C) Because intention is fard according to all schools
D) Because the Salaf stated that no wudu' is valid without intention

Key Takeaway
The necessity of intention in wudu' is grounded in the rationally unintelligible nature of the water's change, demonstrating that physical purification alone does not constitute legal purification without a purposeful act.

Inclusion of Profit with Principal: Prioritizing Essence over Condition
Ruling on attaching profit to principal for zakat with usul rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that essence (al-dhat) takes precedence over temporal condition (al-hal) to determine the zakatability of profit attached to principal.

Core Idea
The profit is essentially connected to its original principal, so it joins for zakat, regardless of the new year's progress.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul presents a fiqh ruling on zakat and unpacks its underlying rationale, serving as a template for usul analysis. The ruling states that profit from the sale of zakatable camels is added to the original principal for zakat purposes even if the new year has not elapsed. The reasoning hinges on the distinction between intrinsic connection (dhat) and temporal condition (hal), with the former prevailing. We will dissect this ruling and its proof to understand how the Hanafi school employs tarjih between competing attributes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Read the passage and note the specific facts: a person sells zakatable camels, uses the proceeds, and makes a profit. The ruling: the profit is attached to the original principal (the camels) for zakat, not to the new investment.
The ruling is explicit: 'ضم الربح إلى أصله وإن بعد عن الحول'.
2
Extract the usul principle
The passage explains the reason: the profit is connected to its principal by essence (dhat) and to the other thousand by condition (hal). 'والذات أحق من الحال' — the essence is more entitled than the condition.
This is a tarjih principle: when two attributes conflict, the intrinsic attribute outweighs the accidental one.
3
Understand the rejection of caution (ihtiyat)
The author notes that caution is not considered in zakat. This means one does not delay zakat out of caution; the ruling is based on definitive connection.
This reinforces that the ruling is not a mere precaution but a solid legal principle.
4
Recognize the passage as a template
The author says these examples are given to serve as a basis for other branches. This passage is not just a fiqh ruling but an usul example for analogical reasoning.
It illustrates how to apply the principle of dhat over hal in other cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن تصرف في ثمن الإبل، فربح ثمن الإبل، فربح ألفاً ضمّ الربح إلى أصله وإن بَعد عن الحول ولا يُعتبر الرجحان بالاحتياط في الزكاة؛ لما قلنا إن الألف الربح متصل بأصله ذاتاً، متصل بالألف الأخرى حالاً، وهي القُرب إلى مضي الحول، والذات أحقُّ من الحال. وإنما ذكرنا من هذه الأقسام أمثلةً معدودة؛ لتكون أصلاً لغيرها من الفروع.
If he disposes of the price of camels, and makes a profit from the price of the camels, and makes a profit of a thousand, the profit is added to its principal even if it is far from the year, and the profit is not considered with caution in zakat; because we said that the thousand profit is connected to its principal in essence, connected to the other thousand in condition, which is the proximity to the passing of the year, and the essence is more entitled than the condition. And we only mentioned from these sections a few examples to serve as a basis for other branches.
Source pages p. 654

Commentary
This passage presents a fiqh ruling with its underlying rationale, used as an example in the usul discussion of tarjih. The ruling: If someone sells zakatable camels and uses the proceeds to buy other camels, any profit made (here a thousand dirhams) is added to the original principal for zakat purposes, even if the new year has not yet been completed. The reasoning: The profit (the thousand) is essentially connected to the original capital (it arose from it) and only temporally connected to the other thousand (the new principal) by proximity to the completion of the year. Since the essence (al-dhat) takes precedence over the temporal condition (al-hal), the profit is attached to the original principal and zakat is due on the combined amount. The author notes that caution (al-ihtiyat) is not considered in zakat, meaning that one does not delay zakat out of caution. This example is one of several given to illustrate the principles of tarjih, serving as a foundation for analogous cases.

Key Terms
الذات (al-dhat): The essence or intrinsic connection of the profit to the original principal from which it arose.
الحال (al-hal): The condition or temporal circumstance, specifically the proximity of the profit to the completion of the zakat year on the new principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the zakat example, what is the ruling regarding the profit from the sale of camels?
A) It is not included in zakat until a new year passes.
B) It is added to the principal regardless of the time remaining in the year.
C) It is zakatable only if the sale was made within the year.
D) It is exempt from zakat.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when an attribute of essence (dhat) conflicts with an attribute of condition (hal), the essence prevails — as applied here to attach profit to its original principal for zakat.

Intention in Purification: Wudu vs Tayammum
Hanafi rebuttal of Shafi'i claim that intention is required for wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that intention is not a condition for the validity of purification, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the distinction between purification by nature and by legislation.

Core Idea
Intention is needed for reward, not for purification — water cleans by nature; worship is additional.

This passage from Al-Bazdawi's Usul tackles a fundamental usul dispute: Is intention (niyyah) a condition for the validity of wudu? The Shafi'i school argues that wudu is an act of worship, hence intention is required. The Hanafi school counters that wudu serves both as purification and worship, and the purification aspect — like washing off impurity — functions through water's natural property, not intention. Understanding this distinction is key to Hanafi usul al-fiqh methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
State the Shafi'i claim and the Hanafi counterclaim about intention in wudu. The issue is whether intention is a condition for validity or only for reward.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof
How does the author argue that water purifies by nature (bi-tab'ihi) and why does intention not affect the purification? Look at the analogy to washing impurity (ghusl al-najas).
3
Examine the counterexample: tayammum
Why does tayammum require intention initially? How does the author distinguish it from wudu? Earth is not naturally a purifier, so intention is needed to make it a purifier.
4
Understand the legal consequence (thamarah)
What is the practical difference in rulings? A Hanafi may pray with a wudu performed without intention; a Shafi'i would require repetition.
5
Apply the principle to a new scenario
If someone performs wudu without intention (e.g., to cool off) and then prays, is the prayer valid according to each school? Use the two-aspect framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والبدن عن النجاسة، فيضطر إلى بيان فقه المسألة، وهو أن الوضوء تطهير ؛ لأنه لا يُعقل بالعين نجاسةٌ فكان كالتيمم في شرط النية لتحقق التعبد، بخلاف غسل النجس. ونحن نقول : إن الماء في هذا الباب عامل بطبعه، وكان القياس غسل كل البدن؛ لأن مخرج النجاسة غير موصوف بالحدث، وإنما البدن موصوف به ، فوجب غسل كله إلا أن الشرع اقتصر على أطراف البدن الأربعة التي هي مثل حدود البدن وأمهاته في هذا المعنى ؛ تيسيراً فيما يكثر وقوعه، ويُعتاد تكراره وأقر على القياس فيما لا حرج فيه، وهو المني، ودم الحيض والنفاس، فلم يكن التعدي عن موضع الحدث إلا قياساً، وإنما يُعنى بالنص الذي لا يُعقل وصف محل الغسل من الطهارة إلى الخبث، فأما الماء فعامل بطبعه والنية للفعل القائم بالماء، لا للوصف القائم بالمحل فكان مثل غسل النجس. بخلاف التراب ؛ لأنه لم يُعقل مطهراً، وإنما صار مطهراً عند إرادة الصلاة، وبعد صحة الإرادة وصيرورته مطهراً يستغني عن النية أيضاً، ومَسْحُ الرأس مُلحَقِّ بالغَسل ؛ لقيامه مقامه، وانتقاله إليه بضرب من الحرج، فثبت أن النية لا تُشترط للتطهير، ولا يجوز أن تشترط لتصير ية ؛ لأنا نسلَّم أن النية لتصير قُربةً شرطٌ ؛ لكنا لا نُسلّم أنه لم يُشرع إلا قربة ، بل شرع بوصف القربة، وبوصف التطهير أيضاً، كغسل الثوب. والصلاة تستغني في ذلك عن وصف القُربة، وإنما تحتاج في ذلك إلى وصف التطهير حتى إن مَن توضأ للنفل : صلى به الفرائض، ومَن توضأ للفرض : صلى به غيره.
And the body from impurity, so one is compelled to explain the fiqh of the issue: that wudu is purification, because impurity is not perceived by the eye, so it was like tayammum in requiring intention for the realization of worship, unlike washing off impurity. And we say: water in this chapter acts by its nature, and the analogy would be washing the entire body because the exit of impurity is not described with hadath, rather the body is described with it, so washing all of it was obligatory, except that the law confined it to the four limbs of the body, which are like the boundaries and roots of the body in this meaning, as a facilitation in what frequently occurs and is habitually repeated. And it upheld analogy in what involves no difficulty, which is semen and blood of menstruation and postpartum, so the deviation from the place of hadath was only by analogy. Rather, it means by the text that the description of the place of washing from purity to impurity is not rational. As for water, it acts by its nature, and intention is for the action residing in water, not for the description residing in the place, so it was like washing off impurity. Unlike earth, because it was not understood as a purifier, and only became a purifier when intending prayer, and after the validity of the intention and its becoming a purifier, it becomes free of intention as well. And wiping the head is attached to washing because it stands in its place, and its transfer to it involves a kind of difficulty. So it is established that intention is not a condition for purification, and it cannot be condition to make it... because we concede that intention is a condition for making it a good deed, but we do not concede that it was legislated only as a good deed; rather it was legislated with the description of good deed and with the description of purification as well, like washing a garment. And prayer is independent of the description of good deed in this regard, and only needs the description of purification, so that whoever performs wudu for a supererogatory prayer may pray obligatory prayers with it, and whoever performs wudu for an obligatory prayer may pray other prayers with it.
Source pages p. 667

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi rebuttal of the Shafi'i position that intention (niyyah) is a condition for the validity of wudu. The author argues that wudu is both purification and worship, but intention is not required for the purification aspect because water purifies by its natural property, just as washing off impurity (ghusl al-najas) does not require intention. The law limited wudu to four limbs for ease, but for semen and menstrual blood, the full-body wash remains by analogy. Tayammum is different because earth is not naturally a purifier; it becomes purifier only when intended for prayer, so intention is needed initially but then not again. Wiping the head is treated like washing. Thus intention is a condition for the reward (qurba), not for the purification itself, analogous to washing a garment. One who performs wudu for a supererogatory prayer may use it for obligatory prayers, showing the purification is valid without specific intention.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): Intention to perform an act of worship, required for the act to be a qurba (good deed).
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as a substitute for wudu when water is unavailable or harmful.
غسل النجس (ghusl al-najas): Washing off physical impurity (najasa) from the body, which requires no intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is intention not required for the purification aspect of wudu?
A) Because wudu is not an act of worship at all.
B) Because water purifies by its natural property, like washing off impurity.
C) Because the Prophet (saw) never had intention for wudu.
D) Because intention is only required for tayammum.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, intention is a condition for reward (qurba), not for the validity of purification by water, distinguishing wudu from tayammum.
