The Condition That Runs in the Status of a Cause
Explains the distinction between cause and condition and the rule for conditions treated as causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a condition that is treated as a cause in Hanafi liability rulings and apply the three conditions for such treatment.

Core Idea
A condition that removes a preventer and precedes a volitional act not attributed to it is treated as a cause for liability.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, a clear distinction exists between a cause (sabab) and a condition (shart). A cause directly brings about a ruling, while a condition enables the cause to operate by removing a preventer. However, some conditions, due to their connection to the effect and resemblance to causes, are elevated to the status of a cause in liability rulings. This lesson explores the criteria for such treatment and its practical implications through classical examples and an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish cause from condition
Identify that a cause (sabab) is a legally suitable attribute that directly necessitates a ruling, whereas a condition (shart) is a prerequisite that removes a preventer but does not directly cause the ruling.
Example: cutting a waterskin is a condition for liquid flow; the liquid's nature is the cause.
2
Recognize the three conditions for a shart to run as a sabab
A condition is treated as a cause if: (1) a volitional act intervenes after it, (2) the volitional act is not attributed to the condition, and (3) the condition precedes that volitional act.
If the intervening act is involuntary or attributed to the condition, the rule changes.
3
Apply the rule to examples
Work through the examples: cutting a waterskin (condition not cause), unlocking a slave's shackle (condition running as cause but no liability because the slave's volition is the cause), opening a cage door (disputed).
In each case, identify whether the intervening act is volitional and attributed.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Examine the disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding liability for opening a cage or stable door when the animal escapes immediately.
The dispute turns on whether the animal's flight is considered a volitional act or legally negligible (harb).
5
Derive the practical effect (thamarah)
Determine the difference in liability: under the majority view, no liability; under Muhammad, liability if the escape is immediate.
This shows how usul principles directly affect furu' rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك شَقِّ الزَّقِّ شرط للسيلان؛ لأن الزّق كان مانعاً. وكذلك القنديل الثقيلُ : ثِقَله علةٌ للسقوط، وإنما الحَبْلُ مانع، فإذا قطع الحبل: فقد زال المانع ، فعَمِلَ الثَّقَلُ عَمَلَه، فثبت أنه شرط، لكن العلة ليست بصالحة للحكم ؛ لأن الثَّقَلَ طَبْع لا تعدي فيه، والمشي مباحٌ بلا شبهةٍ فلم يصلح أن يُجعل علةً بواسطة الثَّقَل ، وإذا لم يعارض الشرط ما هو علةٌ، وللشرط شَبَهُ بالعلل لما تعلَّق به من الوجود أقيم مَقامَ العلة في ضمان النفس والأموال جميعاً. ولهذا لم يجب على حافر البئر كفارةً، ولم يُحرم الميراث؛ لأنه ليس بمباشرة، فلا يلزمه جزاؤها. قسم وأما وضع الحَجَر ، وإشراعُ الجناح والحائط المائل بعد الإشهاد : فمن القسم. لله الأسباب التي جعلت عللاً في الحكم، على ما مرَّ، لا من هذا - وعلى هذا الأصل قلنا في الغاصب إذا بذر حنطة غيره في أرض غيره : إن الزرع للغاصب وإن كان التغير بطبع الأرض والماء والهواء. وأما الإلقاء فشرط محض، لكن العلة لما كانت معنى مسخَّراً لا اختيار له : لم يصلح علةً مع وجود فعل عن اختيار وإن كان شرطاً، فجعل للشرط حكم العلل. ٣- وأما الشرط الذي له حكم الأسباب فأن يعترض عليه فعل مختار غير منسوب إليه ، وأن يكون سابقاً عليه. وذلك مثل رجلٍ حَلّ قيدَ عبدٍ حتى أَبَقَ: لم يضمن قيمته، باتفاق أصحابنا رحمهم الله ؛ لأن المانع من الإباق هو القيد، فكان حِلَّه إزالةً للمانع، فكان شرطاً في الحقيقة، إلا أنه لما سبق الإباق الذي هو و التلف: نُزِّل منزلة الأسباب، فالسبب مما يتقدم، والشرط مما يتأخر. ثم هو سبب محض؛ لأنه اعترض عليه ما هو علةٌ قائمة بنفسها، غيرُ حادثة بالشرط، وكان هذا كمن أرسل دابة في الطريق، فجالت، ثم أتلفت شيئاً : لم يضمنه المرسل ، إلا أن المرسل صاحب سبب في الأصل، وهذا صاحب شرط جعل مسباً. وإذا انفلتت الدابةُ فأتلفت زرعاً بالنهار : كان هَدَراً. وكذلك بالليل عندنا ؛ لأن صاحب الدابة ليس بصاحب شرط، ولا ولا علة. سبب، وقال أبو حنيفة وأبو يوسف رحمهما الله فيمن فتح باب قفص، فطار الطيرُ، أو باب إصطبل، فخرجت الدابة، فضلت: إنه لا يضمن؛ لأن هذا شرط جرى مجرى السبب لما قلنا وقد اعترض عليه فعل مختار، فبقي الأول سبباً خالصاً ، فلم يجعل التلف مضافاً إليه. بخلاف السقوط في البئر ؛ لأنه لا اختيار له في السقوط، حتى إذا أسقط نفسه : فدمُه ،هدر، كمن مشى على قنطرة واهية وضعت بغير حق، فخُسفت به، أو على موضع رش الماء عليه، عالماً به، فزلق به، فعَطب : هدر دمه ؛ لأن الإلقاء هو العلة، وقد صلح لإضافة الحكم إليه. وقال محمد رحمه الله : طيران الطير هدر شرعاً، وكذلك فعل كل بهيمة، فيجعل كالخارج بلا اختيار وصار كسیلان ما في الزق، فإذا خرج على فور الفتح وجب الضمان على صاحب الشرط.
And likewise, cutting the waterskin is a condition for the flow, because the waterskin was a preventer. And likewise the heavy lamp: its weight is a cause for falling, but the rope is a preventer. When the rope is cut, the preventer is removed, so the weight acts accordingly, so it is established that it is a condition. But the cause is not suitable for the ruling because weight is a nature with no transgression in it, and walking is permissible without any ambiguity, so it is not suitable to be made a cause via the weight. And when the condition does not oppose what is a cause, and the condition has a resemblance to causes due to its connection to existence, it is placed in the status of a cause in liability for both life and property. Hence, the digger of a well is not required to pay expiation, nor is he deprived of inheritance, because it is not direct action, so he is not liable for its penalty. Section: As for placing a stone, and extending a balcony, and a leaning wall after testimony, this falls under the section of the causes that have been made causes in the ruling, as has passed, not of this. And upon this principle we said regarding the usurper who sows another's wheat in another's land: the crop belongs to the usurper, even though the change is by the nature of the land, water, and air. As for the act of sowing, it is a pure condition, but because the cause is a subjugated meaning with no choice, it is not suitable as a cause in the presence of a volitional act, even if it is a condition, so the condition is given the ruling of causes. And as for the condition that has the ruling of causes: that a volitional act intervenes upon it, not attributed to it, and it precedes that act. For example, a man unlocks a slave's shackle and the slave runs away: he does not guarantee his value, by agreement of our companions, may Allah have mercy on them, because the preventer of running away was the shackle, so his unlocking it was a removal of the preventer, so it was a condition in reality. However, since it preceded the running away, which is the loss, it is treated as a cause. For a cause precedes, and a condition follows. Then it is a pure cause because what is a cause subsistent in itself, not created by the condition, intervenes upon it. And this is like one who releases an animal on the road, and it wanders and then destroys something: the releaser is not liable, except that the releaser is the owner of a cause in origin, while this person is the owner of a condition that has been made a cause. And if the animal escapes and destroys a crop by day, it is of no consequence. And likewise at night according to us, because the owner of the animal is not the owner of a condition nor a cause. And Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on them, said regarding one who opens the door of a cage and the bird flies, or the door of a stable and the animal goes out and gets lost: he is not liable, because this is a condition that runs in the status of a cause, as we said, and a volitional act has intervened upon it, so the first remains a pure cause, and the loss is not attributed to it. Unlike falling into a well, because the falling one has no choice in falling, to the extent that if one throws himself into it, his blood is of no consequence, like one who walks on a weak bridge placed without right and collapses with him, or on a place sprayed with water, knowing it, and slips and perishes: his blood is of no consequence, because the throwing is the cause, and it is suitable for attributing the ruling to it. And Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, said: the flight of a bird is legally of no consequence, and likewise every beast's action, so it is made like something that goes out without choice, and becomes like the flow of what is in the waterskin. So if it comes out instantly upon opening, liability is incumbent upon the owner of the condition.
Source pages p. 699

Commentary
This passage is a usul al-fiqh lesson on the distinction between cause (sabab) and condition (shart) in Hanafi rulings on liability (daman). The author begins by illustrating the concept with physical examples: cutting a waterskin is a condition for the liquid to flow; the heavy lamp's weight is a cause for its fall, but the rope is a preventer (mani). Cutting the rope removes the preventer, so the weight acts—thus cutting is a condition. However, the weight as a cause is not legally suitable (salih) because it is a natural attribute (tab') with no transgression (ta'addi), and walking is permissible without ambiguity, so it cannot be made a cause via analogy. Yet, because the condition (cutting) resembles a cause due to its connection to the existence of the effect, it is elevated to the status of a cause (ilat) in liability for life and property. Hence, the digger of a well does not owe kaffarah (expiation) nor is he denied inheritance, as his act is not direct causation (mubasharah). Next, the author distinguishes between conditions that have the status of causes and pure causes. The key rule: a condition is treated as a cause when (1) a volitional voluntary act (fi'l mukhtar) intervenes after it, and (2) the volitional act is not attributed to the condition, and (3) the condition precedes that act. Example: untying a slave's shackle, after which the slave runs away. The untying is a condition removing the preventer; since it precedes the volitional act (the slave's escape), it is treated as a cause, but still the owner of the condition is not liable because the direct cause is the slave's own volition. The passage then discusses the case of releasing an animal that wanders and causes damage: no liability on the releaser. The author contrasts this with falling into a well, where the falling person has no choice, so the well-digger is liable. Finally, a dispute within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that opening a cage door (or stable) and the bird/animal escaping immediately does not impose liability on the opener, because the animal's volition intervenes and the opener's act is a condition, not a cause. Muhammad al-Shaybani argues that the flight of a bird is legally 'harb' (negligible), like an animal's action without choice, so if the bird flies instantly upon opening, the opener is liable. This shows the nuanced application of the cause-condition distinction in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition is something that is necessary for the existence of a ruling but is not the direct cause; it removes a preventer or prepares the ground.
سبب (sabab): A cause is that which directly brings about a ruling; it is an attribute that is legally suitable (salih) to be a 'illa.
علة (illa): A cause in the sense of a legal ratio; it is an effective attribute that necessitates the ruling.
شرط جرى مجرى السبب (shart jara majra al-sabab): A condition that is treated as a cause in liability because it precedes a volitional act that is not attributed to it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), if a person opens a cage door and the bird flies out immediately and is lost, what is the ruling?
A) The opener is liable because opening the cage caused the loss.
B) The opener is not liable because the bird's flight is a volitional act that intervenes.
C) The opener is liable only if the bird was expensive.
D) The opener is not liable unless the cage was locked.

Key Takeaway
A condition that removes a preventer and precedes a volitional act not attributed to it is treated as a cause for liability, but the condition's actor is not liable because the volitional act is the direct cause.

Intellect and Obligation: The Hanafi Position on Those Not Reached by Da'wa
Usul al-Fiqh dispute: Can intellect alone impose taklif?

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether intellect alone imposes taklif and evaluate the Ash'ari/Shafi'i counter-argument using the case of those not reached by da'wa.

Core Idea
Intellect is a light for understanding, not a source of obligation; revelation alone imposes taklif.

This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi addresses a foundational debate: Are human beings accountable to God solely on the basis of intellect, or does accountability require divine revelation? The Ash'aris argue that those who never received the call (da'wa) are excused even for shirk. The Hanafis take a nuanced position: intellect establishes eligibility (ahliyyah) but not obligation. Let us dissect the arguments and understand the Hanafi proof from the case of the mature minor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the schools and their positions
State the Ash'ari position on the person not reached by da'wa (excused even for shirk) and the Hanafi position (not excused if they actively commit kufr, but excused if they remain neutral).
Note the author's criticism that the Ash'ari view 'exceeds the limit'.
2
Trace the Hanafi proof: the murahiqa analogy
Analyze the case of a mature girl who has intellect but does not describe kufr: she is not considered an apostate. This shows that intellect alone does not make one liable for kufr; rather, actual description or belief is needed.
The analogy is drawn directly from al-Jami' al-Kabir.
3
Understand the Hanafi view on 'aql
Explain the definition of 'aql as a light that illuminates but is incapable by itself. Intellect is only a condition for eligibility (ahliyyah), not a cause for obligation (taklif).
The author contrasts the intellect to the sun: it provides light but the eye (heart) must perceive.
4
Examine the opposite extreme: the Shafi'i position on daman
Describe the Shafi'i ruling that people not reached by da'wa are entitled to blood money if killed, implying their kufr is excused. Explain the Hanafi response: they are not ma'sum because we do not make their kufr excused.
The Hanafi ruling denies daman, showing that such people are not treated as protected even if they never heard the message.

Source Text

وقالت الأشعرية فيمن لم تبلغه الدعوة، فغَفَلَ عن الاعتقاد حتى هلك : إنه معذور.
قالوا: ولو اعتقد الشرك، ولم تبلغه الدعوة: إنه معذور أيضاً. وفي هذا الفصل أعني أن يُجعل شركه معذوراً: تجاوز عن الحد، كما تجاوزت المعتزلة عن الحد في الطرف الآخر.
والقول الصحيح في الباب هو قولنا: إن العقل معتبر لإثبات الأهلية، وهو مِن أعزّ النَّعم، خُلِق متفاوتاً في أصل القسمة.
وقد مرَّ تفسيره قبل هذا، أنه نور في بدن الآدمي، مثل الشمس في ملكوت الأرض، يُضيء به الطريق الذي مبدؤه من حيث ينقطع إليه أثر الحواس. ثم هو عاجز بنفسه، وإذا وضح له الطريقُ كان الدَّرَك للقلب بفهمه، كالشمس في الملكوت الظاهرة إذا بَزَغَت، وبدا شعاعها، ووضح الطريق: كانت العين مدركة بشهابها وما بالعقل كفاية بحال في كل لحظة، ولذلك قلنا في الصبي العاقل إنه لا يُكلف بالإيمان، حتى إذا عَقَلَتِ المُراهِقة ولم تَصِفٌ، زوج مسلم بين أبوين مسلمين: لم تُجعل مرتدة، ولم تبن من زوجها، ولو بلغت كذلك : لبانت من زوجها.
وهي تحت ولو عَقَلَت وهي مراهقة، فوصفت الكفر كانت مرتدةً وبانت من زوجها، ذكر ذلك في الجامع الكبير»، فعلم به أنه غير مكلف.
وكذلك نقول في الذي لم تبلغه الدعوة: إنه غير مكلف بمجرد العقل، وإنه إذا لم يصف إيماناً ولا كفراً، ولم يعتقد على شيء كان معذوراً. وإذا وَصَفَ الكفرَ وعَقَدَه ، أو عَقَدَه ولم يصفه: لم يكن معذوراً، وكان من أهل النار مخلداً، على نحو ما وصفنا في الصبي. ومعنى قولنا: إنه لا يُكلَّف بمجرد العقل: نريد به أنه إذا أعانه الله تعالى بالتجربة والهِمَّة وأَمْهَلَه لدَرْك العواقب : لم يكن معذوراً وإن لم تبلغه الدعوة، على نحو ما قاله أبو حنيفة رحمه الله في السفيه إذا بلغ خمساً وعشرين سنة : لم يُمنَع عنه ماله؛ لأنه قد استوفى مدة التجربة والامتحان، فلا بد من أن يزداد به رشداً.
وليس على الحد في هذا الباب دليل قاطع، فمَن جعل العقل حجةً يمتنع الشرع بخلافه فليس معه دليل يعتمد عليه سوى أمورٍ ظاهرة، نُسلّمها له؛ لأنه لم يَرِدْ في الشرع دليل على أن العقل موجب، ولا يجوز أن يكون موجباً وعلة بدون الشرع، إذ العلل موضوعات الشرع، وليس إلى العباد ذلك؛ لأنه يَنزِعُ إلى الشركة.
فمَن جعله موجباً بلا دليل شرعاً : فقد جاوز حد العِنادِ، وحَدَّ الشرع، ومَن ألغاه من كل وجه : فلا دليل له أيضاً.
وهو مذهب الشافعي رحمه الله ، فإنه قال في قوم لم تبلغهم الدعوة إذا قتلوا ضُمِنوا، فَجَعَلَ كفرَهم عَفْواً.
وأصحابنا رحمهم الله قالوا: لا يُضمنون؛ لأنا لا نجعل كفرهم عفواً، فمَن كان فيهم من جملة مَن يُعذَر على ما فسرنا : لم يستوجب عصمة بدون دار الإسلام.
The Ash'aris said about the one whom the call did not reach, and he was heedless of belief until he died: he is excused. They said: even if he believed in shirk, and the call did not reach him: he is also excused. In this chapter, meaning that his shirk is made excused: it is an excess beyond the limit, just as the Mu'tazila exceeded the limit on the other extreme. The correct statement in this chapter is our statement: The intellect is considered for establishing eligibility (ahliyyah), and it is one of the most precious blessings, created with variation in origin of division. Its explanation has already passed before this: that it is a light in the body of the human, like the sun in the earthly realm, lighting the path whose beginning is where the effect of the senses ends. Then it is incapable by itself, and when the path becomes clear to it, the perception is for the heart by its understanding, like the sun in the apparent realm when it rises, its rays appear, and the path becomes clear: the eye perceives with its flame, and the intellect does not have sufficiency in any state at every moment. Therefore we said about the intelligent child that he is not obligated with faith. Even when a girl approaching puberty is intelligent and does not describe (kufr), married to a Muslim between two Muslim parents: she is not made an apostate, and she does not separate from her husband. And had she attained puberty likewise, she would have separated from her husband. And if she was intelligent during her approaching puberty, and she described kufr, she is an apostate and separates from her husband. That is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir. So it is known from this that he is not obligated. Similarly we say about the one whom the call did not reach: he is not obligated by mere intellect. And if he does not describe faith nor kufr, and does not believe in anything, he is excused. And if he described kufr and held it, or held it without describing it, he is not excused, and he is among the people of the Fire, eternally, according to what we described regarding the child. The meaning of our statement: he is not obligated by mere intellect is that if Allah helps him with experience and determination and gives him time to perceive consequences: he is not excused even if the call did not reach him, according to what Abu Hanifa said about the foolish one if he reaches twenty-five years: his wealth is not prevented from him; because he has completed the period of experience and testing, so he must have increased in maturity by it. There is no decisive proof on the boundary in this chapter. So whoever makes the intellect a proof, such that the law cannot contradict it, he has no reliable proof besides apparent matters, which we concede to him; because no proof has come in the law that the intellect is a cause, and it is not permissible that it be a cause (mujib) and 'illa without the law, for the 'ills are the subject matters of the law, and this is not for the servants; because it tends towards partnership. So whoever makes it a cause without a legal proof has surpassed the limit of obstinacy and the limit of the law. And whoever negates it completely also has no proof. And this is the madhhab of al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, for he said about a people whom the call did not reach: if they are killed, they are guaranteed (daman), so he made their kufr excused. And our companions, may Allah have mercy on them, said: they are not guaranteed; because we do not make their kufr excused. So whoever among them is of the category of those who are excused according to what we explained: he does not deserve protection (isma) without Dar al-Islam.
Source pages p. 708

Commentary
This passage addresses a key usul dispute: whether intellect alone imposes legal obligation (taklif) without divine revelation. The Ash'aris hold that a person who never received the da'wa is excused, even if they commit shirk. The author deems this excessive, just as the Mu'tazila went to the other extreme (holding intellect sufficient for obligation). The correct Hanafi view is that intellect is only a condition for eligibility (ahliyyah), not a cause for obligation. Intellect is a light that guides but is inherently deficient; it cannot independently impose duties. The proof is the case of a mature minor (murahiqa) who has intellect but does not describe kufr: she is not considered an apostate when married to a Muslim, but if she explicitly describes kufr, she becomes an apostate. Similarly, a person not reached by da'wa is not obligated by intellect alone, but if they describe kufr or hold kufr in their heart, they are blameworthy. Abu Hanifa's ruling on the foolish person reaching 25 years shows that experience and time can create accountability even without explicit da'wa. The author then refutes those who treat intellect as an independent source of obligation (mujib), stating that there is no decisive proof for that, and such a view essentially makes humans partners in legislation. The Shafi'i view that those not reached by da'wa are entitled to blood money (daman) if killed implies their kufr is excused. Hanafis deny this: such people do not deserve protection (isma) unless they are in Dar al-Islam, because their kufr is not excused. Thus, intellect is a means, not a cause; obligation comes from revelation alone.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): A light in the human body that illuminates the path of understanding, but is incapable by itself and needs divine guidance.
التكليف (al-taklif): Legal obligation that requires a basis in revelation; not imposed solely by intellect.
الدعوة (al-da'wa): The invitation to Islam, i.e., the message of the prophets reaching a person.
الأهلية (al-ahliyyah): Legal capacity or eligibility; intellect establishes this, but actual obligation requires revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, what is the ruling for a mature girl (murahiqa) who has intellect (aqalat) but does not describe kufr and is married to a Muslim?
A) She is considered a murtadda and separates from her husband.
B) She is not considered a murtadda and remains married.
C) She is considered a kafira but remains married.
D) She is separated only if she explicitly states kufr.

Key Takeaway
Intellect is a condition for eligibility, not a cause for obligation; only revelation can impose taklif.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Intellect as a Condition for Legal Capacity
Debating intellect as cause or condition for legal capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that intellect is a condition for legal capacity, not a cause, and apply it to determine liability in the case of those not reached by the prophetic call.

Core Idea
Intellect is a condition, not a cause; only sharia establishes causes for rulings.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh clarifies the precise role of intellect ('aql) in legal capacity (ahliyyah). The Hanafi school insists that intellect alone cannot be a cause (illa) for rulings because causes are established only by divine revelation. Instead, intellect is a quality or condition for capacity. The practical consequence emerges in the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i over whether people who never received the prophetic call are liable for murder. By the end of this lesson, you will grasp the legal logic behind the Hanafi position and be able to trace its usul roots.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim
Locate the author's statement that 'he is not obligated by mere intellect' (لا يكلَّف بمجرد العقل). This is the thesis: intellect alone does not impose obligation.
Reflect on what 'obligation' (taklif) requires beyond intellect.
2
Understand the condition vs. cause distinction
The author argues that there is no definitive proof (dalil qati) that intellect is a cause. Causes are subject matters of sharia (علل موضوعات الشرع), not human constructs. Intellect, as a quality of ahliyyah, is a condition (shart) for capacity, not a cause.
A cause (illa) is an effective reason that brings about a ruling; a condition must be present for the ruling to apply but does not produce it.
3
Examine the Shafi'i counter-example
The Shafi'i madhhab holds that people not reached by the call are liable for murder (if they kill) because their disbelief is considered excused (afw). This implies that intellect alone can ground accountability.
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in liability.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis reject making disbelief excused. Those who do not describe or hold disbelief are excused, but others are not. Without abode of Islam (Dar al-Islam), there is no protection. Intellect, mixed with desire (hawa), cannot be a reliable proof.
The Hanafi position is that accountability requires additional factors: da'wa or experiential maturity (as in the safih example).
5
Synthesize the usul principle
Conclude that intellect is among the qualities (sifat) of ahliyyah, not a cause. The attribution of rulings to causes is only a facilitation from Allah; causes themselves are not inherently effective.
This lesson establishes a foundational Hanafi usul principle: 'al-illah must be from sharia.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنه إذا لم يصف إيماناً ولا كفراً، ولم يعتقد على شيء كان معذوراً. وإذا وَصَفَ الكفرَ وعَقَدَه ، أو عَقَدَه ولم يصفه: لم يكن معذوراً، وكان من أهل النار مخلداً، على نحو ما وصفنا في الصبي. ومعنى قولنا: إنه لا يُكلَّف بمجرد العقل: نريد به أنه إذا أعانه الله تعالى بالتجربة والهِمَّة وأَمْهَلَه لدَرْك العواقب : لم يكن معذوراً وإن لم تبلغه الدعوة، على نحو ما قاله أبو حنيفة رحمه الله في السفيه إذا بلغ خمساً وعشرين سنة : لم يُمنَع عنه ماله؛ لأنه قد استوفى مدة التجربة والامتحان، فلا بد من أن يزداد به رشداً.

وليس على الحد في هذا الباب دليل قاطع، فمَن جعل العقل حجةً يمتنع الشرع بخلافه فليس معه دليل يعتمد عليه سوى أمورٍ ظاهرة، نُسلّمها له؛ لأنه لم يَرِدْ في الشرع دليل على أن العقل موجب، ولا يجوز أن يكون موجباً وعلة بدون الشرع، إذ العلل موضوعات الشرع، وليس إلى العباد ذلك؛ لأنه يَنزِعُ إلى الشركة.

قتلوا ضُمِنوا، فَجَعَلَ كفرَهم عَفْواً.
وأصحابنا
رحمهم الله قالوا: لا يُضمنون؛ لأنا لا نجعل كفرهم عفواً،
فمَن كان فيهم من جملة مَن يُعذَر على ما فسرنا : لم يستوجب عصمة بدون

و
وذلك لأنه لا يجد في الشرع أن العقلَ غيرُ مُعتَبَرٍ للأهلية، فإنما يُلغيه
بطريق دلالة الاجتهاد والمعقول، فيتناقض مذهبه ، وإن العقل لا ينفك عن الهوى، فلا يصلح حجة بنفسه بحال.
وإنما وجبت نسبة الأحكام إلى العلل ؛ تيسيراً على العباد من غير أن تكون عللاً بذواتها، وأن يُجعل العقل علةً بنفسه وهو باطن: فيه حرجٌ عظيم، فلم يجز ذلك، والله أعلم.
وإذا ثبت أن العقل من صفات الأهلية : قلنا إن الكلام في هذا الباب ينقسم إلى قسمين: الأهلية والأمور المعترضة على الأهلية.
And if he does not describe faith nor disbelief, and does not hold a belief on anything, he is excused. And if he described disbelief and held it as a belief, or held it without describing it, he is not excused, and he is from the people of hell, eternally, as we described in the child. And the meaning of our saying: he is not obligated by mere intellect: we intend by it that if Allah helps him with experience and determination and gives him time to realize consequences, he is not excused even if the call has not reached him, as Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, said concerning the foolish person when he reaches twenty-five years old: his wealth is not prevented from him; because he has completed the period of experience and testing, so he must have increased in maturity.
Obligatory? And
And there is no definitive proof on the limit in this chapter. So whoever makes intellect a proof that sharia cannot contradict has no proof to rely on except apparent matters, which we concede to him; because no proof has come in sharia that intellect is a cause, and it is not permissible for it to be a cause without sharia, for causes are subject matters of sharia, and that is not up to the servants; because it tends towards partnership.
So whoever makes it a cause without a sharia proof has transgressed the limit of obstinacy and the limit of sharia, and whoever nullifies it entirely also has no proof.
And it is the madhhab of al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, for he said concerning a people whom the call has not reached: if they kill, they are liable, so he made their disbelief excused.
And our companions, may Allah have mercy on them, said: they are not liable; because we do not make their disbelief excused, so whoever among them is from those who are excused as we explained does not deserve protection without the abode of Islam.
And that is because he does not find in sharia that intellect is not considered for legal capacity, so he nullifies it by way of indication of ijtihad and reasoning, so his madhhab is contradictory. And indeed, intellect is not free from desire, so it is not suitable as a proof by itself at all.
And the attribution of rulings to causes was only made necessary as a facilitation for the servants, not that they are causes in themselves. And to make intellect a cause by itself while it is hidden: there is great difficulty in it, so that is not permissible. And Allah knows best.
And when it is established that intellect is among the qualities of legal capacity, we say: the discussion in this chapter is divided into two parts: legal capacity and the obstacles that oppose legal capacity.

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh addresses the role of intellect ('aql) in legal capacity (ahliyyah) and whether it serves as a cause (illa) for rulings. The author begins by clarifying when a person is excused for disbelief: if one neither describes nor holds a belief in anything, they are excused. However, if one describes disbelief or holds it as a belief, they are not excused and are eternally in hell. This parallels the case of a child. The author then elaborates that the statement 'he is not obligated by mere intellect' means that if Allah grants a person experience and the ability to consider consequences, he is not excused even without receiving the prophetic call (da'wa). Abu Hanifa's ruling on the foolish person (safih) reaching twenty-five years is cited: his wealth is not withheld because he has completed the period of experience and should have attained maturity.

The passage then enters a usul debate. The author argues that there is no definitive proof (dalil qati) that intellect is a cause for rulings. Those who make intellect a proof that cannot be contradicted by sharia rely only on apparent matters, but no textual evidence supports that intellect is a cause. Causes are established by sharia, not by human reasoning, as that would imply partnership with the divine. Making intellect a cause without a proof transgresses sharia, while completely nullifying intellect also lacks proof.

The Shafi'i position is mentioned: for people not reached by the call, if they kill, they are liable (i.e., they are not excused due to ignorance), thus considering their disbelief as an excuse (afw). The Hanafi position, from Abu Hanifa's companions, is that they are not liable because their disbelief is not considered an excuse. Among them, those who are excused (as per the earlier criteria) are not protected without being in Dar al-Islam.

The author then critiques the opposing view: they cannot find in sharia that intellect is irrelevant for ahliyyah, so they nullify it through ijtihad and reasoning, which creates a contradiction. Intellect is not free from desire (hawa), so it cannot serve as a standalone proof. The attribution of rulings to causes is a facilitation for people, not because causes are inherently effective. Making intellect a cause itself, which is hidden, would cause great hardship, so it is not permissible.

Finally, the author establishes that intellect is among the qualities (sifat) of legal capacity (ahliyyah). Thus, the discussion in this chapter is divided into two parts: ahliyyah itself and the obstacles that impede ahliyyah (al-umur al-mu'taridah 'ala al-ahliyyah).

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): Intellect; a quality of legal capacity (ahliyyah) that allows understanding and responsibility.
الأهلية (al-ahliyyah): Legal capacity; the fitness of a person to acquire rights and obligations.
العلة (al-'illah): A cause or effective reason for a ruling, established by sharia, not by human intellect alone.
العفو (al-'afw): Excuse or pardon; here, treating disbelief as excused due to ignorance of the call.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on a person who has not received the prophetic call and kills someone?
A) They are liable and must pay blood money.
B) They are not liable because their disbelief is excused.
C) They are not liable as long as they did not describe or hold disbelief.
D) They are considered Muslims and thus liable.

Key Takeaway
Intellect is a condition for legal capacity, not a cause; only sharia establishes causes, so accountability requires da'wa or experiential maturity.

Legal Capacity (Ahliyyah): Definition, Proof, and Application
Define and subdivide legal capacity with proofs and applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define legal capacity (ahliyyah), distinguish its two types, explain the Hanafi basis of capacity for obligation on dhimma, and apply the rule to determine when a minor is liable for obligations in huquq al-ibad and huquq Allah.

Core Idea
Legal capacity is rooted in the primordial dhimma, making every human suitable for obligation from birth.

This passage from the Usul of al-Bazdawi lays out the foundational Hanafi concept of legal capacity (ahliyyah). It divides capacity into two types: capacity for obligation (ahliyyat wujub) and capacity for performance (ahliyyat ada'). The former is based on the dhimma, a legal personality established by the primordial covenant mentioned in the Quran. The passage then explores the implications: a minor has capacity for obligation, but whether an obligation actually binds depends on whether its ruling can be meaningfully applied. This yields a nuanced classification of rights that affect a minor's liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Types of Legal Capacity
Read the opening sentence: 'al-ahliyyatu darban: ahliyyat wujub wa ahliyyat ada'. Understand that capacity for obligation is about being subject to rights and duties, while capacity for performance is about validly executing legal acts.
The passage focuses mostly on ahliyyat wujub; ahliyyat ada is mentioned but not elaborated.
2
Trace the Basis of Ahliyyat Wujub: Dhimma
The author states that ahliyyat wujub is based on dhimma, and that every human is born with a dhimma suitable for obligation, by consensus. Locate the Quranic proofs (7:172, 17:13) that establish this primordial covenant.
Dhimma is a legal construct, not physical; it allows the minor to have rights and obligations even if not yet fully realized.
3
Understand the Division of Huquq al-Ibad
The passage divides the rights of servants into compensatory (ghurm, 'iwad), maintenance-like (nafaqa), and penal (punishments, blood money). For each, determine whether the minor is liable based on whether the ruling (hukm) can be achieved through delegation or requires personal capacity.
The key criterion: if the obligation's purpose can be fulfilled by a guardian (e.g., paying money), it binds the minor; if it requires personal deterrence (e.g., blood money), it does not.
4
Apply the Same Logic to Huquq Allah
The passage summarizes that for rights of Allah, obligation is binding whenever the ruling is sound in application. If the ruling cannot be applied (e.g., fasting for a child), the obligation is void despite the cause existing.
This shows that capacity for obligation is not absolute; it is conditioned on the possibility of fulfilling the ruling.
5
Synthesize the Overall Framework
Now combine: All humans have ahliyyat wujub from birth due to dhimma, but actual liability depends on the nature of the obligation. This framework resolves apparent contradictions (e.g., why minors can incur debts but not criminal penalties).
This is a practical tool for a mufti when assessing obligations on minors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأهلية ضربان:
١ - أهلية وجوب.
٢- وأهلية أداء.
أما أهلية الوجوب فتنقسم فروعُها ، وأصلها واحد، وهو الصلاح للحكم، فمن كان أهلاً لحكم الوجوب بوجه: كان أهلاً للوجوب، ومن لا فلا.
* وأهلية الأداء نوعان:
١ - كامل يصلح للزوم العهدة.
٢ - وقاصر لا يصلح للزوم العهدة.
أما أهلية الوجوب : فبناء على قيام الذمة، وأن الآدمي يُولد وله ذمةٌ صالحة للوجوب، بإجماع الفقهاء رحمهم الله ؛ بناء على العهد الماضي. قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذْ أَخَذَ رَبُّكَ مِن بَنِي ءَادَمَ مِن ظُهُورِهِمْ ذُرِّيَّهُمْ وَأَشْهَدَهُمْ عَلَى أَنفُسِهِمْ ... الآية، الأعراف/ ١٧٢.
وقال تعالى: ﴿ وَكُلَّ إِنسَنِ أَلْزَمْنَاهُ طَائِرَهُ فِي عُنُقِهِ ) الإسراء / ١٣.
والذمة : العهد، وإنما يراد به نفس ورقبة لها ذمة وعهد، حتى إن ولي الصبي إذا اشترى للصبي شيئاً كما ولد لزمه الثمن، وقبل الانفصال هو : جزء من وجه فلم تكن له ذمة مطلقة حتى صلح ليجب له الحق، ولم يجب عليه.
وإذا انفصل، فظهرت ذمته مطلقةً كان أهلاً بذمته للوجوب، غير أن الوجوب غير مقصود بنفسه، فيجوز أن يبطل الوجوب؛ لعدم حكمه وغرضه، فكما ينعدم الوجوبُ لعدم محله مع قيام السبب: فكذلك يجوز ينعدم لعدم حكمه أيضاً، فيصير هذا القسم منقسماً بانقسام الأحكام، وقد مر التقسيم قبل هذا في أول الفصل.
فأما في حقوق العباد فما كان منها غُرْماً وعوضاً: فالصبي من أهل وجوبه ؛ لأن حكمه وهو أداء العين يحتمل النيابة ؛ لأن المال مقصود، لا الأداء، فوجب القول بالوجوب عليه متى صح سببه.
وما كان صلةٌ لها شَبَهُ بالمُؤَن، وهي نفقة الزوجات والقرابات: لزمه أيضاً ، أما نفقة الزوجات فلها شَبَهُ بالأعواض ، وأما الأخرى فمونة اليسار. وكل صلة لها شبه بالأجر: لم يكن الصبي من أهله، مثل تحمل العقل؛ لأنه لا يخلو عن صفة الجزاء مقابلاً بالكف عن الأخذ على يد الظالم، ولذلك اختص به رجال العشائر، دون النساء.
وما كان عقوبةً، أو جزاء : لم يجب عليه، على ما مرَّ؛ لأنه لا يصلح لحكمه، فبطل القول بلزومه.
وكذلك القول في حقوق الله تعالى على الإجمال: إن الوجوب لازم متى صح القول بحكمه، ومتى بطل القولُ بحكمه: بطل القول بوجوبه وإن سببه ومحله ؛ لأن الوجوب كما ينعدم مرةً لعدم سببه، ومرةً لعدم حكمه.
Legal capacity is of two types: 1. Capacity for obligation. 2. Capacity for performance. As for capacity for obligation, its branches are divided, but its origin is one, which is suitability for ruling. So whoever is suitable for a ruling of obligation in any way is suitable for obligation, and whoever is not, is not. * Capacity for performance is of two types: 1. Complete, suitable for binding liability. 2. Deficient, not suitable for binding liability. As for capacity for obligation, it is based on the existence of the dhimma (covenant), and that a human is born with a dhimma suitable for obligation, by consensus of the jurists (may Allah have mercy on them), based on the past covenant. Allah Almighty said: 'And when your Lord took from the children of Adam, from their loins, their descendants and made them testify of themselves...' [Al-A'raf 172]. And He said: 'And every human We have fastened his fate to his neck' [Al-Isra' 13]. And dhimma means covenant, and what is meant is a self and a neck that has a dhimma and covenant, such that when the guardian of a minor buys something for the minor, like [a purchase] at birth, the price becomes binding on him. Before separation (from the mother), he is a part of a face, so he does not have an absolute dhimma such that he is suitable for a right to be established for him, and it is not binding on him. When he separates, his dhimma becomes absolute, so he is suitable by his dhimma for obligation. However, obligation is not intended for its own sake, so it is permissible for obligation to be nullified due to the absence of its ruling and purpose. Just as obligation is non-existent due to the absence of its locus despite the existence of the cause, similarly it can become non-existent due to the absence of its ruling as well. So this section is divided according to the division of rulings, and the division was mentioned before at the beginning of the chapter. As for the rights of servants: whatever is a debt and compensation, the minor is capable of its obligation because its ruling, which is payment of the property, admits delegation, for the property is intended, not the payment, so the obligation is affirmed on him whenever its cause is sound. Whatever is a gift that resembles maintenance, such as alimony for wives and relatives, it is also binding on him. As for alimony for wives, it resembles compensations; as for others, it is the expense of wealth. Every gift that resembles a reward, the minor is not capable of it, such as bearing blood money, because it is not free from the quality of punishment, in exchange for refraining from taking the hand of the oppressor, and therefore it is specific to clan men, not women. Whatever is a punishment or a penalty, it is not binding on him, as mentioned, because he is not suitable for its ruling, so the statement of its binding is invalid. Similarly, regarding the rights of Allah Almighty in summary: obligation is binding whenever its ruling is sound in application, and whenever the ruling is invalid in application, the statement of its obligation is invalid, even if its cause and locus exist, because obligation is non-existent sometimes due to the absence of its cause, and sometimes due to the absence of its ruling.
Source pages p. 711

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of legal capacity (ahliyyah) from the Hanafi usul tradition. The author divides ahliyyah into two primary types: ahliyyat wujub (capacity to have obligations) and ahliyyat ada' (capacity to perform legal acts). Ahliyyat wujub is underpinned by the concept of dhimma (the legal personality or covenant) which every human possesses from birth, as proven by Quranic verses (7:172 and 17:13) and consensus. This capacity allows a minor to have rights and obligations, but the fulfilment of obligations may be suspended until they become practicable. The author then subdivides the effects of ahliyyat wujub based on the nature of the obligation. For rights of servants (huquq al-ibad), obligations that are compensatory (ghurm and 'iwad) are binding on a minor because the goal is property, which can be managed through a guardian. Maintenance (nafaqa) for spouses and relatives is also binding, either because it resembles compensation or due to necessity. However, obligations that are penal or punitive (like blood money 'aql) are not binding on minors because they cannot fulfil the intended deterrent purpose. Similarly, for rights of Allah, the obligation is binding if the ruling can be meaningfully applied; if not, the obligation lapses despite the cause being present. This shows the Hanafi emphasis on the practical applicability of rulings based on capacity.

Key Terms
أهلية (ahliyyah): Legal capacity: the quality by virtue of which one becomes suitable for legal rulings (ahkam).
ذمة (dhimma): The legal personality or covenant that makes one subject to rights and obligations; established from birth based on the primordial covenant.
حقوق العباد (huquq al-'ibad): Rights of individuals (private rights) such as debts, compensation, maintenance, and blood money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following obligations is a minor NOT liable for?
A) A debt for groceries bought by the guardian on the minor's behalf.
B) Maintenance for the minor's wife (if married).
C) Blood money ('aql) for unintentional killing.
D) Payment for a necessary surgery.

Key Takeaway
Legal capacity for obligation exists from birth, but actual liability depends on whether the ruling can be meaningfully applied to the minor.

The Minor's Eligibility for Obligation: General Principle and Rights of Humans
Parsing the minor's obligation in human rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three factors (cause, subject, effect) that determine the absence of obligation and apply them to classify various human rights as binding or not on a minor.

Core Idea
Obligation can be absent due to absence of cause, subject, or effect; the minor is obligated for compensations and maintenance, but not for penal gifts.

In this passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul, we explore how the minor's capacity for obligation varies depending on the nature of the right. The author establishes a general analytical framework: obligation ceases not only when its cause or subject is absent, but also when its intended effect (performance) cannot be realized. This framework is then applied to different categories under the rights of humans.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three absences
Recognize that obligation can be absent due to lack of cause (sabab), subject (mahall), or effect (hukm). The effect is performance (ada').
2
Analyze compensations ('iwad and ghurm)
For these, the purpose is the wealth itself, not the personal act of delivery; delegation is possible, so the minor is obligated.
Example: if a minor buys something, the price is binding.
3
Analyze maintenance (nafaqa)
Maintenance for wives and relatives is also binding because it resembles compensation in some respects.
The text distinguishes between spousal maintenance (like compensations) and other relatives (like expense of the wealthy).
4
Analyze penal gifts (silah with shabah al-jizya)
These, like blood money, have a penal character; the minor is not eligible because performance (bearing the penalty) is not feasible.
Blood money is specific to men of clans, not women.
5
Identify the pattern
The key distinction is whether the obligation's effect can be achieved through proxy (niyaba) or requires personal capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصبي إذا اشترى للصبي شيئاً كما ولد لزمه الثمن، وقبل الانفصال هو : جزء من وجه فلم تكن له ذمة مطلقة حتى صلح ليجب له الحق، ولم يجب عليه.
وإذا انفصل، فظهرت ذمته مطلقةً كان أهلاً بذمته للوجوب، غير أن الوجوب غير مقصود بنفسه، فيجوز أن يبطل الوجوب؛ لعدم حكمه وغرضه، فكما ينعدم الوجوبُ لعدم محله مع قيام السبب: فكذلك يجوز ينعدم لعدم حكمه أيضاً، فيصير هذا القسم منقسماً بانقسام الأحكام، وقد مر التقسيم قبل هذا في أول الفصل.
فأما في حقوق العباد فما كان منها غُرْماً وعوضاً: فالصبي من أهل وجوبه ؛ لأن حكمه وهو أداء العين يحتمل النيابة ؛ لأن المال مقصود، لا الأداء، فوجب القول بالوجوب عليه متى صح سببه.
وما كان صلةٌ لها شَبَهُ بالمُؤَن، وهي نفقة الزوجات والقرابات: لزمه أيضاً ، أما نفقة الزوجات فلها شَبَهُ بالأعواض ، وأما الأخرى فمونة اليسار. وكل صلة لها شبه بالأجزية : لم يكن الصبي من أهله، مثل تحمل العقل؛ لأنه لا يخلو عن صفة الجزاء مقابلاً بالكف عن الأخذ على يد الظالم، ولذلك اختص به رجال العشائر، دون النساء.
وما كان عقوبةً، أو جزاء : لم يجب يجب عليه، على ما مرَّ؛ لأنه لا يصلح لحكمه، فبطل القول بلزومه.
وكذلك القول في حقوق الله تعالى على الإجمال: إن الوجوب لازم متى صح القول بحكمه، ومتى بطل القولُ بحكمه: بطل القول بوجوبه وإن سببه ومحله ؛ لأن الوجوب كما ينعدم مرةً لعدم سببه، ومرةً لعدم محله، فينعدم أيضاً لعدم حكمه، وقد مرَّ تفسير هذه الجملة أيضاً. فأما الإيمان: فلا يجب على الصبي قبل أن يعقل ؛ لما قلنا من عدم أهلية الأداء.
وكذلك العبادات الخالصة المتعلقة بالبدن أو بالمال: لا تجب عليه وإن وُجد سببها ومحلّها؛ لعدم الحكم، وهو الأداء؛ لأن الأداء هو المقصود في حقوق الله تعالى، وذلك فعل يحصل عن اختيار على سبيل التعظيم ؛ تحقيقاً للابتلاء، والصِّغَرُ ينافيه.
وما يتأدى بالنائب: لا يصلح طاعةً ؛ لأنها نيابةُ جَبْرِ، لا اختيار، فلو ذلك : لصار المالُ مقصوداً، وذلك باطل في جنس القُرَب، وجب مع
فلذلك لم تلزمه الزكاة والصلاة والحج والصوم.
وما يشوبه معنى المؤنة مثل صدقة الفطر : لم يلزمه عند محمد رحمه الله؛ لما قلنا، ولزمه عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف رحمهما الله؛ اجتزاء بالأهلية القاصرة والاختيار القاصر، وذلك بواسطة الولي.
ولزمه ما كان مؤنة في الأصل، وهو العُشر والخراج ؛ لما ذكرنا.
وما كان عقوبةً : لم يجب أصلاً ؛ لعدم حكمه ، ولهذا كان الكافر أهلاً لأحكام لا يُراد بها وجه الله تعالى؛ لأنه أهل لأدائها، فكان أهلاً للوجوب له، وعليه.
ولما لم يكن أهلاً لثواب الآخرة لم يكن أهلا لوجوب شيء من
الشرائع التي طاعات الله تعالى عليه وكان الخطاب بها موضوعا عنه
عندنا.
هي
The minor: if he purchases something for the minor, just as he is born, the price is binding upon him. And before separation (from the mother) he is part of the mother, so he does not have an absolute legal capacity (dhimma) such that a right can be established for him, nor is anything obligatory upon him. And when he separates, his absolute legal capacity appears, and he becomes eligible through his legal capacity for obligation. However, obligation is not intended for its own sake; so it is permissible that obligation be nullified due to the absence of its effect (hukm) and purpose. Just as obligation ceases due to the absence of its subject (mahall) while the cause exists, similarly it may cease due to the absence of its effect. So this category becomes divided according to the division of rulings, and the division has preceded earlier in the beginning of the chapter. As for the rights of humans: whatever among them is a compensation (ghurm) and consideration ('iwad), the minor is eligible for its obligation, because its effect, which is the delivery of the object, can be delegated (because wealth is intended, not the act of delivery). So obligation is affirmed upon him whenever its cause is sound. And whatever is a gift (silah) that resembles maintenance (mu'an), such as the maintenance of wives and relatives, it is also binding upon him. As for the maintenance of wives, it resembles compensations; as for the other (relatives), it is the expense of the wealthy. And every gift that resembles penal compensation (jizya') — the minor is not eligible for it, such as bearing the blood money ('aql), because it is not free from the quality of penalty, being in exchange for refraining from taking the hand of the oppressor; therefore it is specific to the men of clans, not women. And whatever is a punishment or penalty is not obligatory upon him, as has passed, because he is not fit for its effect, so the statement of its binding is invalid. Similarly, the statement concerning the rights of God in summary: obligation is binding whenever its effect is sound; and whenever the statement of its effect is invalid, the statement of its obligation is invalid, even if its cause and subject exist, because obligation can cease due to absence of its cause, or absence of its subject, and also due to absence of its effect. The explanation of this summary has also preceded. As for faith (iman), it is not obligatory upon the minor before he attains reason, due to what we said of the lack of capacity for performance. Similarly, pure acts of worship related to body or wealth are not obligatory upon him, even if their cause and subject exist, due to the absence of the effect, which is performance, because performance is the purpose in the rights of God, and that is an act done with choice in the manner of veneration, to achieve trial, and minority contradicts that. And what can be performed by proxy is not valid as an act of obedience, because it is a proxy of compulsion, not choice; if that were so, wealth would become the purpose, and that is invalid in the category of devotional acts. Therefore, zakat, prayer, hajj, and fasting are not binding upon him. And what is mixed with the meaning of maintenance, like sadaqat al-fitr: it is not binding upon him according to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) for what we said; but it is binding according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them), deeming sufficient the deficient capacity and deficient choice through the guardian. And what is originally maintenance, such as 'ushr (tithe) and kharaj (land tax), is binding upon him for what we mentioned. And whatever is a punishment is not obligatory at all, due to the absence of its effect. For this reason, the disbeliever is eligible for rulings by which the face of Allah is not intended, because he is eligible to perform them, so he is eligible for obligation in his favor and against him. And since he is not eligible for the reward of the hereafter, he is not eligible for the obligation of any of the laws (shara'i') that are acts of obedience to Allah, and the address (khitab) concerning them is removed from him in our view.
Source pages p. 712

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul discusses the eligibility (ahliyya) of the minor (sabi) for legal obligation (wujub). The author first sets out the general principle: obligation can be absent due to the absence of its cause (sabab), its subject (mahall), or its effect (hukm). The effect of obligation is performance (ada'), which is the intended purpose. For the minor, before birth (while still a part of the mother), he has no absolute legal capacity (dhimma mulaqa). After birth, his dhimma becomes absolute, but obligation is not automatically binding; it depends on whether the effect (performance) can be realized. The author then divides rights into categories: rights of humans (huquq al-'ibad) and rights of God (huquq Allah). In rights of humans, compensations (ghurm and 'iwad) are obligatory on the minor because the purpose is the wealth, not the personal act of delivery, so delegation is possible. Maintenance (nafaqa) for wives and relatives is also obligatory, resembling compensation. However, gifts resembling penal compensation (like blood money) are not obligatory because they carry a penal element that the minor cannot bear. Punishments are not obligatory. In rights of God, pure acts of worship (iman, salah, zakat, hajj, sawm) are not obligatory on the minor because performance requires choice and understanding, which the minor lacks. Acts that can be performed by proxy are not valid as obedience because proxy here would be compulsory, not voluntary. Sadaqat al-fitr (charity of breaking the fast) is disputed: Imam Muhammad says it is not obligatory because it resembles maintenance, but Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say it is obligatory through the guardian (wali) due to the deficient capacity of the minor. Tithe ('ushr) and land tax (kharaj) are obligatory as they are originally maintenance obligations. The passage ends with a comparison to the disbeliever (kafir): the disbeliever is eligible for worldly rulings (financial obligations, etc.) because he can perform them, but not for purely devotional obligations intended for divine reward, as he lacks the capacity for reward in the hereafter.

Key Terms
الوجوب (al-wujub): Legal obligation; a ruling that can be absent due to absence of cause, subject, or effect (performance).
الأداء (al-ada'): Performance of an obligation; the intended effect (hukm) of wujub, especially in rights of God.
أهلية الوجوب (ahliyyat al-wujub): Eligibility for obligation; the quality by which a person becomes subject to legal duties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bazdawi, which of the following is NOT a reason for obligation to cease?
A) Absence of cause
B) Absence of subject
C) Absence of intention
D) Absence of effect

Key Takeaway
The minor's obligation depends not only on cause and subject but crucially on whether the intended effect (performance) can be realized, which varies by the nature of the right.

The Minor's Eligibility for Obligation: Rights of God and the Sadaqat al-Fitr Dispute
Parsing the minor's obligation in divine rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between pure acts of worship and those mixed with maintenance, and state the positions of the three Hanafi imams on sadaqat al-fitr for a minor.

Core Idea
Pure worship requires personal performance; the minor is exempt. Mixed obligations like sadaqat al-fitr are disputed among the imams.

This lesson continues the analysis of the minor's eligibility for obligation, now focusing on the rights of God. The passage distinguishes pure devotional acts from those that have a dimension of maintenance, leading to a famous intra-Hanafi dispute on sadaqat al-fitr. Understanding this distinction is key to applying the usul principle correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify pure acts of worship
These are bodily and financial acts like salah, zakat, hajj, sawm. The text says they are not obligatory because performance requires choice and understanding.
The minor lacks ahliyyat al-ada' for these.
2
Explain why prayer and zakat are not binding
Performance is the intended effect; it requires intent and capacity, which the minor lacks. Proxy (niyaba) is not valid here because it would be compulsion, not voluntary worship.
The text contrasts with human rights where wealth is the purpose.
3
Identify mixed acts like sadaqat al-fitr
This resembles maintenance (mu'na). The text presents a dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold it obligatory via guardian; Muhammad holds it not obligatory.
4
Understand the dispute
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf accept deficient capacity and deficient choice through the guardian. Muhammad argues it is like maintenance and the minor is not eligible.
The text does not give tarjih.
5
Identify purely maintenance acts like 'ushr and kharaj
These are binding because they are originally maintenance (mu'na) and do not require personal devotion.
They are treated like human rights compensations.

الصبي إذا اشترى للصبي شيئاً كما ولد لزمه الثمن، وقبل الانفصال هو : جزء من وجه فلم تكن له ذمة مطلقة حتى صلح ليجب له الحق، ولم يجب عليه.
وإذا انفصل، فظهرت ذمته مطلقةً كان أهلاً بذمته للوجوب، غير أن الوجوب غير مقصود بنفسه، فيجوز أن يبطل الوجوب؛ لعدم حكمه وغرضه، فكما ينعدم الوجوبُ لعدم محله مع قيام السبب: فكذلك يجوز ينعدم لعدم حكمه أيضاً، فيصير هذا القسم منقسماً بانقسام الأحكام، وقد مر التقسيم قبل هذا في أول الفصل.
فأما في حقوق العباد فما كان منها غُرْماً وعوضاً: فالصبي من أهل وجوبه ؛ لأن حكمه وهو أداء العين يحتمل النيابة ؛ لأن المال مقصود، لا الأداء، فوجب القول بالوجوب عليه متى صح سببه.
وما كان صلةٌ لها شَبَهُ بالمُؤَن، وهي نفقة الزوجات والقرابات: لزمه أيضاً ، أما نفقة الزوجات فلها شَبَهُ بالأعواض ، وأما الأخرى فمونة اليسار. وكل صلة لها شبه بالأجزية : لم يكن الصبي من أهله، مثل تحمل العقل؛ لأنه لا يخلو عن صفة الجزاء مقابلاً بالكف عن الأخذ على يد الظالم، ولذلك اختص به رجال العشائر، دون النساء.
وما كان عقوبةً، أو جزاء : لم يجب يجب عليه، على ما مرَّ؛ لأنه لا يصلح لحكمه، فبطل القول بلزومه.
وكذلك القول في حقوق الله تعالى على الإجمال: إن الوجوب لازم متى صح القول بحكمه، ومتى بطل القولُ بحكمه: بطل القول بوجوبه وإن سببه ومحله ؛ لأن الوجوب كما ينعدم مرةً لعدم سببه، ومرةً لعدم محله، فينعدم أيضاً لعدم حكمه، وقد مرَّ تفسير هذه الجملة أيضاً. فأما الإيمان: فلا يجب على الصبي قبل أن يعقل ؛ لما قلنا من عدم أهلية الأداء.
وكذلك العبادات الخالصة المتعلقة بالبدن أو بالمال: لا تجب عليه وإن وُجد سببها ومحلّها؛ لعدم الحكم، وهو الأداء؛ لأن الأداء هو المقصود في حقوق الله تعالى، وذلك فعل يحصل عن اختيار على سبيل التعظيم ؛ تحقيقاً للابتلاء، والصِّغَرُ ينافيه.
وما يتأدى بالنائب: لا يصلح طاعةً ؛ لأنها نيابةُ جَبْرِ، لا اختيار، فلو ذلك : لصار المالُ مقصوداً، وذلك باطل في جنس القُرَب، وجب مع
فلذلك لم تلزمه الزكاة والصلاة والحج والصوم.
وما يشوبه معنى المؤنة مثل صدقة الفطر : لم يلزمه عند محمد رحمه الله؛ لما قلنا، ولزمه عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف رحمهما الله؛ اجتزاء بالأهلية القاصرة والاختيار القاصر، وذلك بواسطة الولي.
ولزمه ما كان مؤنة في الأصل، وهو العُشر والخراج ؛ لما ذكرنا.
وما كان عقوبةً : لم يجب أصلاً ؛ لعدم حكمه ، ولهذا كان الكافر أهلاً لأحكام لا يُراد بها وجه الله تعالى؛ لأنه أهل لأدائها، فكان أهلاً للوجوب له، وعليه.

The minor: if he purchases something for the minor, just as he is born, the price is binding upon him. And before separation (from the mother) he is part of the mother, so he does not have an absolute legal capacity (dhimma) such that a right can be established for him, nor is anything obligatory upon him. And when he separates, his absolute legal capacity appears, and he becomes eligible through his legal capacity for obligation. However, obligation is not intended for its own sake; so it is permissible that obligation be nullified due to the absence of its effect (hukm) and purpose. Just as obligation ceases due to the absence of its subject (mahall) while the cause exists, similarly it may cease due to the absence of its effect. So this category becomes divided according to the division of rulings, and the division has preceded earlier in the beginning of the chapter. As for the rights of humans: whatever among them is a compensation (ghurm) and consideration ('iwad), the minor is eligible for its obligation, because its effect, which is the delivery of the object, can be delegated (because wealth is intended, not the act of delivery). So obligation is affirmed upon him whenever its cause is sound. And whatever is a gift (silah) that resembles maintenance (mu'an), such as the maintenance of wives and relatives, it is also binding upon him. As for the maintenance of wives, it resembles compensations; as for the other (relatives), it is the expense of the wealthy. And every gift that resembles penal compensation (jizya') — the minor is not eligible for it, such as bearing the blood money ('aql), because it is not free from the quality of penalty, being in exchange for refraining from taking the hand of the oppressor; therefore it is specific to the men of clans, not women. And whatever is a punishment or penalty is not obligatory upon him, as has passed, because he is not fit for its effect, so the statement of its binding is invalid. Similarly, the statement concerning the rights of God in summary: obligation is binding whenever its effect is sound; and whenever the statement of its effect is invalid, the statement of its obligation is invalid, even if its cause and subject exist, because obligation can cease due to absence of its cause, or absence of its subject, and also due to absence of its effect. The explanation of this summary has also preceded. As for faith (iman), it is not obligatory upon the minor before he attains reason, due to what we said of the lack of capacity for performance. Similarly, pure acts of worship related to body or wealth are not obligatory upon him, even if their cause and subject exist, due to the absence of the effect, which is performance, because performance is the purpose in the rights of God, and that is an act done with choice in the manner of veneration, to achieve trial, and minority contradicts that. And what can be performed by proxy is not valid as an act of obedience, because it is a proxy of compulsion, not choice; if that were so, wealth would become the purpose, and that is invalid in the category of devotional acts. Therefore, zakat, prayer, hajj, and fasting are not binding upon him. And what is mixed with the meaning of maintenance, like sadaqat al-fitr: it is not binding upon him according to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) for what we said; but it is binding according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them), deeming sufficient the deficient capacity and deficient choice through the guardian. And what is originally maintenance, such as 'ushr (tithe) and kharaj (land tax), is binding upon him for what we mentioned. And whatever is a punishment is not obligatory at all, due to the absence of its effect. For this reason, the disbeliever is eligible for rulings by which the face of Allah is not intended, because he is eligible to perform them, so he is eligible for obligation in his favor and against him. And since he is not eligible for the reward of the hereafter, he is not eligible for the obligation of any of the laws (shara'i') that are acts of obedience to Allah, and the address (khitab) concerning them is removed from him in our view.
Source pages p. 712

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul discusses the eligibility (ahliyya) of the minor (sabi) for legal obligation (wujub). The author first sets out the general principle: obligation can be absent due to the absence of its cause (sabab), its subject (mahall), or its effect (hukm). The effect of obligation is performance (ada'), which is the intended purpose. For the minor, before birth (while still a part of the mother), he has no absolute legal capacity (dhimma mulaqa). After birth, his dhimma becomes absolute, but obligation is not automatically binding; it depends on whether the effect (performance) can be realized. The author then divides rights into categories: rights of humans (huquq al-'ibad) and rights of God (huquq Allah). In rights of humans, compensations (ghurm and 'iwad) are obligatory on the minor because the purpose is the wealth, not the personal act of delivery, so delegation is possible. Maintenance (nafaqa) for wives and relatives is also obligatory, resembling compensation. However, gifts resembling penal compensation (like blood money) are not obligatory because they carry a penal element that the minor cannot bear. Punishments are not obligatory. In rights of God, pure acts of worship (iman, salah, zakat, hajj, sawm) are not obligatory on the minor because performance requires choice and understanding, which the minor lacks. Acts that can be performed by proxy are not valid as obedience because proxy here would be compulsory, not voluntary. Sadaqat al-fitr (charity of breaking the fast) is disputed: Imam Muhammad says it is not obligatory because it resembles maintenance, but Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say it is obligatory through the guardian (wali) due to the deficient capacity of the minor. Tithe ('ushr) and land tax (kharaj) are obligatory as they are originally maintenance obligations. The passage ends with a comparison to the disbeliever (kafir): the disbeliever is eligible for worldly rulings (financial obligations, etc.) because he can perform them, but not for purely devotional obligations intended for divine reward, as he lacks the capacity for reward in the hereafter.

Key Terms
الوجوب (al-wujub): Legal obligation; a ruling that can be absent due to absence of cause, subject, or effect (performance).
الأداء (al-ada'): Performance of an obligation; the intended effect (hukm) of wujub, especially in rights of God.
أهلية الوجوب (ahliyyat al-wujub): Eligibility for obligation; the quality by which a person becomes subject to legal duties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is sadaqat al-fitr not binding upon a minor according to Imam Muhammad?
A) Because it is a pure act of worship.
B) Because it resembles maintenance and the minor is not eligible.
C) Because the minor has no wealth.
D) Because the guardian is exempt.

Key Takeaway
In divine rights, pure worship requires personal performance and is not obligatory on minors, but maintenance-like obligations and those with a penal character are treated differently, with an intra-Hanafi dispute on mixed cases.

Obligation and Capacity: Pure Worship Not Required of Minors
Explaining the rulings of obligation for minors and disbelievers based on capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi concept of ahliyyat al-ada' (capacity for performance) to determine whether a minor is obligated to perform pure acts of worship like prayer and zakat.

Core Idea
Pure worship requires personal performance; a minor lacks capacity, so no obligation.

This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi explores why minors are not obligated to perform pure acts of worship. The key is the Hanafi distinction between capacity for obligation (ahliyyat al-wujub) and capacity for performance (ahliyyat al-ada'). Understanding this helps one see how obligations that require intention and choice are handled in the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key concept: ahliyyat al-ada'
Find where the passage mentions 'ahliyyat al-ada' and understand that it means the ability to perform an act with choice and intention.
This capacity is a prerequisite for pure worship obligations.
2
Distinguish pure worship from mixed obligations
Note that pure worship (ibadat khalisa) is not obligatory on a minor; but acts mixed with maintenance (like sadaqat al-fitr) have differing rulings. Also, worldly obligations (ushr, kharaj) are obligatory.
The distinction hinges on whether the act's primary purpose is worship or worldly benefit.
3
Analyze the internal Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that sadaqat al-fitr is obligatory on a minor via the guardian; Imam Muhammad disagrees. Understand the reasoning: deficient capacity vs. no real performance.
This is an example of how different assessments of capacity lead to different rulings.
4
Apply the principle to other cases
The passage extends the same logic to the disbeliever (no obligation for worship), the menstruating woman (fasting obligatory, prayer not), and the insane person (obligation lifts if hardship persists).
Hardship (haraj) plays a role in lifting obligation.

Source Text

فأما الإيمان: فلا يجب على الصبي قبل أن يعقل؛ لما قلنا من عدم أهلية الأداء. وكذلك العبادات الخالصة المتعلقة بالبدن أو بالمال: لا تجب عليه وإن وُجد سببها ومحلّها؛ لعدم الحكم، وهو الأداء؛ لأن الأداء هو المقصود في حقوق الله تعالى، وذلك فعل يحصل عن اختيار على سبيل التعظيم؛ تحقيقاً للابتلاء، والصِّغَرُ ينافيه. وما يتأدى بالنائب: لا يصلح طاعةً؛ لأنها نيابةُ جَبْرِ، لا اختيار، فلو ذلك لصار المالُ مقصوداً، وذلك باطل في جنس القُرَب، فلذلك لم تلزمه الزكاة والصلاة والحج والصوم. وما يشوبه معنى المؤنة مثل صدقة الفطر: لم يلزمه عند محمد رحمه الله؛ لما قلنا، ولزمه عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف رحمهما الله؛ اجتزاء بالأهلية القاصرة والاختيار القاصر، وذلك بواسطة الولي. ولزمه ما كان مؤنة في الأصل، وهو العُشر والخراج؛ لما ذكرنا. وما كان عقوبةً: لم يجب أصلاً؛ لعدم حكمه. ولهذا كان الكافر أهلاً لأحكام لا يُراد بها وجه الله تعالى؛ لأنه أهل لأدائها، فكان أهلاً للوجوب له، وعليه. ولما لم يكن أهلاً لثواب الآخرة لم يكن أهلا لوجوب شيء من الشرائع التي طاعات الله تعالى عليه وكان الخطاب بها موضوعاً عنه عندنا. ولزمه الإيمان بالله تعالى لما كان أهلاً لأدائه، ووجوب يُجعل مخاطباً بالشرائع بشرط تقديم الإيمان؛ لأنه رأس أسباب أهلية أحكام نعيم الآخرة، فلم يصلح أن يُجعل شرطاً مقتضى. وقد قال بعض مشايخنا رحمهم الله بوجوب كل الأحكام والعبادات على الصبي؛ لقيام الذمة، وصحة الأسباب، ثم السقوط بعذر الحرج. قال الشيخ: وقد كنا عليه مدةً، لكنَّا تركناه بهذا القول الذي اخترناه، وهذا أسلم الطريقين صورة ومعنى، وتقليداً وحجة. ولذلك قلنا في الصبي إذا بلغ في بعض شهر رمضان: إنه لا يقضي ما مضى. وكذلك نقول في الحائض إن الصوم يلزمها؛ لاحتمال الأداء، ثم النقل إلى البدل، وهو القضاء؛ لأن الحرج لما عُدم في ذلك بقي الحكم، فوجب القول بالوجوب. وأما الصلاة فقد بطل الأداء؛ لما فيه من الحرج، فبطل الوجوب؛ لعدم حكمه مع قيام محل الوجوب، وقيام سببه. وكذلك قولنا في الجنون إذا امتد، فصار لزوم الأداء يؤدي إلى الحرج، فبطل القولُ بالأداء، وبطل القولُ بالوجوب؛ لعدم الحكم أيضاً. في الصلاة والصيام معاً، وإذا لم يمتد في شهر رمضان لزمه أصله؛ لاحتمال حكمه. وإذا عقل الصبي واحتمل الأداء: قلنا بوجوب أصل الإيمان، دون أدائه حتى صح الأداء، وذلك لما عُرف أن الوجوب جبر من الله تعالى.
As for faith: it is not obligatory upon the minor before he understands; because of what we said of the lack of capacity for performance. And likewise pure acts of worship related to the body or wealth: they are not obligatory upon him even if their cause and locus exist; due to the absence of the ruling, which is performance; because performance is the intended purpose in the rights of Allah Almighty, and that is an action performed by choice in a manner of veneration, realizing the test, and childhood contradicts that. What is performed by a deputy is not considered obedience; because it is a compulsory deputyship, not by choice; if that were so, wealth would become the objective, and that is invalid in the category of devotions. Therefore, zakat, prayer, hajj, and fasting are not obligatory upon him. As for what is mixed with the meaning of maintenance, such as sadaqat al-fitr: it is not obligatory upon him according to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him); due to what we said, and it is obligatory upon him according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them); accepting the deficient capacity and deficient choice, through the guardian. And what was originally maintenance, i.e., tithe and land tax, is obligatory upon him; due to what we mentioned. As for what is a penalty: it is not obligatory at all; due to the absence of its ruling. Hence the disbeliever is qualified for rulings not intended for the sake of Allah; because he is qualified to perform them, so he is qualified for obligation for them and upon him. Since he is not qualified for the reward of the Hereafter, he is not qualified for the obligation of any of the laws that are acts of obedience to Allah upon him, and the address regarding them is removed from him according to us. And faith in Allah is obligatory upon him because he is qualified to perform it; and obligation is made addressing him with the laws on condition of prior faith; because it is the primary cause of qualification for the rulings of the bliss of the Hereafter, so it cannot be made a condition necessitating. Some of our teachers (may Allah have mercy on them) said that all rulings and acts of worship are obligatory upon the minor; due to the establishment of liability and the validity of causes, then they drop due to the excuse of hardship. The teacher said: we used to hold this for a time, but we abandoned it for this opinion which we chose; and this is the safer of the two paths in form and meaning, and in emulation and proof. Therefore, we said regarding the minor if he reaches puberty during part of Ramadan: he does not make up what has passed. Likewise, we say regarding the menstruating woman: fasting is obligatory upon her; due to the possibility of performance, then transfer to the substitute, which is qada'; because when hardship is absent in that, the ruling remains, so obligation is necessary. As for prayer: performance is invalidated; due to the hardship in it, so obligation is invalidated; due to the absence of its ruling despite the existence of the locus of obligation and its cause. Likewise, our statement regarding insanity if it persists, such that the necessity of performance leads to hardship: the statement of performance is invalidated, and the statement of obligation is invalidated; due to the absence of the ruling as well. In prayer and fasting together. And if it does not persist in Ramadan, the original is obligatory upon him; due to the possibility of its ruling. When the minor understands and can potentially perform, we say: the origin of faith is obligatory, but not its performance until performance is sound; because it is known that obligation is a compulsion from Allah Almighty.
Source pages p. 713

Commentary
This passage is a usul al-fiqh discussion on the conditions for obligation (wujub) and performance (ada') regarding legal capacity (ahliyya). It opens by stating that faith (iman) is not obligatory upon a minor before he reaches the age of understanding (‘aql), because the capacity for performance (ahliyyat al-ada') is absent. The author then extends this principle: all pure acts of worship (ibadat khalisa), whether bodily or financial, are not obligatory on a minor even if their cause (sabab) and locus (mahall) exist, because performance is the intended purpose in the rights of Allah, and performance requires choice and intention, which childhood negates. Acts that can be performed by a deputy (na’ib) are not considered valid acts of obedience because deputyship in such cases is compulsory (niyabat jabar), not voluntary; if it were allowed, the wealth would be the goal, which is invalid in devotions. Thus, zakat, prayer, hajj, and fasting are not obligatory on a minor. However, for acts mixed with maintenance (mu’na), like sadaqat al-fitr, there is a difference of opinion: Imam Muhammad holds they are not obligatory, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold they are obligatory by accepting deficient capacity through the guardian. Land tax (ushr and kharaj), being originally maintenance, are obligatory on a minor. Penalties (uqubat) are not obligatory at all due to absence of their ruling. The discussion then turns to the disbeliever (kafir): he is qualified for rulings not intended for the sake of Allah (like worldly transactions) because he can perform them; but he is not qualified for acts of worship that bring reward, so those obligations are removed from him. Faith is obligatory upon him because he can perform it. The author then mentions a view of some mashayikh that all obligations apply to the minor but drop due to hardship, but the author prefers the safer view that obligations do not apply. Practical applications follow: a minor who reaches puberty during Ramadan does not have to make up missed fasts; a menstruating woman is obligated to fast (and make up); prayer is not obligatory for her due to hardship; and provisions for insanity. Finally, when a minor understands and can potentially perform, the origin of faith is obligatory but not its performance until actual ability.

Key Terms
أهلية الأداء (ahliyyat al-ada'): The legal capacity to perform an act with choice and intention, required for the obligation of acts of worship
العبادات الخالصة (al-ibadat al-khalisa): Pure acts of worship solely for Allah, not mixed with any worldly purpose
نيابة جبر (niyabat jabar): Compulsory deputyship, where a guardian performs an act on behalf of another without the latter's choice

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is zakat not obligatory upon a minor?
A) Because the minor has no wealth.
B) Because the capacity for performance (ahliyyat al-ada') is absent.
C) Because the cause (sabab) of zakat is missing.
D) Because the minor is not a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
A minor is not obligated to perform pure acts of worship (prayer, fasting, zakat, hajj) due to lack of capacity for performance (ahliyyat al-ada'), but obligations mixed with worldly maintenance may be imposed through a guardian.
