Distinguishing Wujub from Ada': Hanafi Usul on Obligation and Hardship
Usul rule: Distinction between obligation and performance based on hardship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between wujub and ada' in Hanafi usul and apply the principle of haraj to determine when obligation falls off for minors, menstruating women, and the insane.

Core Idea
Obligation (wujub) is based on capacity, not burden; hardship (haraj) removes performance, not necessarily obligation.

This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi explores a foundational Hanafi principle: obligation (wujub) is distinct from performance (ada'). The author argues that a minor is obligated to have faith because he can understand it, but not obligated to perform all sharia acts until puberty. He then applies this to fasting, prayer, menstruation, insanity, and unconsciousness, showing how the presence or absence of hardship determines whether obligation remains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core distinction
Understand that wujub is a divine imposition based on capacity and cause, while ada' is the actual performance requiring address (khitab) and ability. Wujub can exist without immediate ada'.
This is key: a minor can be obligated to believe (iman) without being addressed for other acts.
2
Apply the concept of haraj (hardship)
Recognize that continuous hardship (e.g., prolonged insanity) can invalidate both ada' and wujub; temporary hardship (e.g., menstruation) only delays ada' via qada'.
Hardship is the criterion that determines whether obligation remains or falls off.
3
Work through the examples
Trace the rulings for: minor reaching puberty in Ramadan (no qada'), menstruating woman (obligation of fasting remains), prolonged insanity (both wujub and ada' fall), temporary insanity (qada' required).
Each example illustrates the interplay of wujub, ada', and haraj.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some earlier scholars held all obligations apply to minors but fall due to haraj; the author prefers the safer view that minors are not addressed at all.
The chosen view simplifies: no khitab means no wujub for most acts before puberty.
5
Derive the usul rule
Formulate the principle: wujub is binding upon capacity, but performance requires absence of hindrance. Hardship that prevents performance may negate wujub if continuous; otherwise, wujub remains, and qada' is required.
This rule is used in later fatwa for similar cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولزمه الإيمان بالله تعالى لما كان أهلاً لأدائه، ولم يجعل مخاطباً بالشرائع بشرط تقديم الإيمان؛ لأنه رأس أسباب أهلية أحكام نعيم الآخرة، فلم يصلح أن يجعل شرطاً مقتضى. وقد قال بعض مشايخنا رحمهم الله بوجوب كل الأحكام والعبادات على الصبي؛ لقيام الذمة، وصحة الأسباب، ثم السقوط بعذر الحرج. قال الشيخ: وقد كنا عليه مدةً، لكنَّا تركناه بهذا القول الذي اخترناه، وهذا أسلم الطريقين صورة ومعنى، وتقليداً وحجة. مضى. ولذلك قلنا في الصبي إذا بلغ في بعض شهر رمضان: إنه لا يقضي ما فاته، وكذلك نقول في الحائض إن الصوم يلزمها؛ لاحتمال الأداء، ثم النقل إلى البدل، وهو القضاء؛ لأن الحرج لما عُدم في ذلك بقي الحكم، فوجب القول بالوجوب. وأما الصلاة فقد بطل الأداء؛ لما فيه من الحرج، فبطل الوجوب؛ لعدم حكمه مع قيام محل الوجوب، وقيام سببه. وكذلك قولنا في الجنون إذا امتد، فصار لزوم الأداء يؤدي إلى الحرج، فبطل القولُ بالأداء، وبطل القولُ بالوجوب؛ لعدم الحكم أيضاً. في الصلاة والصيام معاً، وإذا لم يمتد في شهر رمضان لزمه هذا أصله؛ لاحتمال حكمه. وإذا عقل الصبي واحتمل الأداء: قلنا بوجوب أصل الإيمان، دون أدائه حتى صح الأداء، وذلك لما عُرف أن الوجوب جبر من الله تعالى بأسباب وضعت للأحكام، إذا لم يَخلُ الوجوب عن حكمه، وليس في الوجوب تكليف وخطاب، وإنما ذلك في الأداء. ولا خطاب ولا تكليف على الصبي بمجرد العقل حتى يبلغ، فثبت أنه غير مخاطب بالإيمان، لكن صحة الأداء تُبتنى على كون الشيء مشروعاً، وعلى قدرة الأداء، لا على الخطاب والتكليف كالمسافر يؤدي الجمعة من غير خطاب ولا تكليف. والإغماء لما لم يناف حكم وجوب الصوم: لم يناف وجوبه، وكان منافياً لحكم وجوب الصلاة إذا امتد، فكان منافياً لوجوبه. والنومُ لمَّا لم يكن منافياً لحكم الوجوب إذا انتبه: لم يكن منافياً للوجوب أيضاً، والله أعلم.
And belief in Allah is obligatory upon him (the minor) because he is capable of performing it, and he is not made addressed by the laws (sharia) with the condition of first having belief, because it is the head of causes of capacity for the rulings of the bliss of the afterlife, so it is not suitable to be made a conditional requirement. And some of our teachers (may Allah have mercy on them) said that all rulings and acts of worship are obligatory upon the minor, because of the existence of liability (dhimma) and the validity of causes, then they fall off due to the excuse of hardship. The teacher (al-Shaykh) said: We used to hold that view for a while, but we abandoned it for this statement which we have chosen, and this is the safer of the two ways in form and meaning, in following and in proof. It passed. Therefore we say regarding the minor if he reaches puberty during part of Ramadan: he does not make up what he missed, and similarly we say regarding the menstruating woman that fasting is obligatory upon her, because of the possibility of performance (ada'), then transfer to the substitute (badal), which is making up (qada'), because when hardship is absent in that, the ruling remains, so it is necessary to say obligation. As for prayer, performance is invalidated because of the hardship in it, so obligation is invalidated because of its ruling not existing along with the locus of obligation and its cause existing. And similarly our saying regarding insanity if it is prolonged, then the necessity of performance leads to hardship, so the statement of performance is invalidated, and the statement of obligation is invalidated due to lack of ruling also. In prayer and fasting together. And if it is not prolonged in Ramadan, it is necessary for him to make up this origin due to the possibility of its ruling. And if the minor has intellect and possibility of performance: we say obligation of the foundation of belief, without its performance until performance becomes valid, and that is because it is known that obligation is a compulsion from Allah Almighty by means placed for rulings, since obligation is not empty of its ruling, and there is no burden and address in obligation; that is only in performance. And there is no address and burden upon the minor by mere intellect until he reaches puberty, so it is established that he is not addressed with belief, but validity of performance is built on the thing being prescribed and on capacity for performance, not on address and burden, like the traveler performing Friday prayer without address and burden. And unconsciousness, since it does not negate the ruling of obligation of fasting, it does not negate its obligation, and it was negating the ruling of obligation of prayer if prolonged, so it negated its obligation. And sleep, since it is not negating the ruling of obligation if one awakens, it is also not negating obligation. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 714

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and discussion on the nature of obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. The author begins by stating that a minor who has intellect must have belief (iman) because he is capable of performing it, but he is not addressed with the entire sharia until he first has belief. Some Hanafi scholars held that all obligations apply to minors because they have a valid dhimma (legal personality) and the causes of obligation are present, but they fall off due to hardship. The author prefers the view that obligations do not apply to minors due to lack of address (khitab). This is safer. Then the author applies this principle to specific cases: if a minor reaches puberty during Ramadan, he does not need to make up the missed fasts because at the time of the fast he was not obligated. A menstruating woman, however, must make up fasts because she is a legally responsible person and the hardship of fasting during menses is temporary; since she can perform the fast later (qada), obligation remains. For prayer, the obligation falls off completely because the hardship is in the very act of prayer during menses (impurity). Similarly, prolonged insanity removes both the obligation and performance of prayer and fasting because the hardship is continuous. But if insanity is temporary (e.g., part of Ramadan), make-up is required because the capacity for performance exists after sanity returns. The passage then distinguishes between obligation (wujub) and performance (ada'). Obligation is a divine imposition based on the person being capable of the act; it is not a burden (taklif) or address (khitab) in itself. Performance requires both the act being legislated and the person having actual ability. The minor is not addressed until puberty, but may still validly perform acts like belief because they are prescribed and he has ability. Unconsciousness (ighma') does not negate the obligation of fasting because it does not contradict the ruling (hukm) of obligation (i.e., the fast can be made up), but prolonged unconsciousness negates the obligation of prayer because the act of prayer cannot be performed at all. Sleep, being temporary and natural, does not negate obligation when one awakens.

Key Terms
الوجوب (al-wujub): A legal obligation that is binding but distinct from performance; it is a divine imposition based on capacity and does not necessarily require actual performance at the time.
الأداء (al-ada'): Actual performance of an act of worship or legal duty, requiring the person to be addressed (mukhatab) and free from preventing excuses.
الحرج (al-haraj): Extreme hardship or difficulty that causes the obligation to fall off or be postponed.
الجبر (al-jabr): Compulsion; in the passage, obligation is described as a 'jabr' from Allah, meaning a legal imposition based on causes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a minor reaches puberty during Ramadan, what is the ruling regarding the fasts he missed before puberty?
A) He must make up all missed fasts because he now has the capacity.
B) He does not make up any missed fasts because he was not obligated before puberty.
C) He must make up the missed fasts only if he had reached the age of discernment.
D) He must fast the remaining days and make up the missed ones after Ramadan.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, wujub is distinct from ada'; a person may be obligated (e.g., to believe) without being addressed for performance, and hardship determines whether performance or even obligation is removed.

Obligation Exists Without Address: A Hanafi Usul Rule
Explaining that wujub is separate from khitab and taklif

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that wujub is independent of khitab and taklif, and distinguish between obligation and performance in cases like minors, travelers, unconsciousness, and sleep.

Core Idea
Obligation (wujub) exists without address; performance requires address and capacity.

This passage draws a sharp line between obligation itself and the legal burden to perform. The Hanafi school asserts that an act can be obligatory without the person being addressed or burdened, a distinction that has profound implications for the validity of acts performed by minors, those unconscious, and others. Understanding this rule prevents the common error of conflating the existence of an obligation with the capacity to fulfill it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Claim
Locate the sentence where the author states that obligation (wujub) is separate from address (khitab) and burden (taklif).
The key phrase: 'ليس في الوجوب تكليف وخطاب'.
2
Analyze the Minor and Traveler Examples
Examine how the author uses the minor who is not addressed yet can perform valid acts, and the traveler who may perform Friday prayer without being obligated. Note what makes performance valid: legislation (mashru') and capacity (qudrah), not address.
3
Apply to States of Unconsciousness and Sleep
Work through the author's reasoning: unconsciousness does not negate obligation of fasting (if it ends) but does negate prayer obligation if prolonged; sleep does not negate obligation. Understand the logic: the ruling of obligation persists unless the condition (e.g., consciousness for prayer) is permanently absent.
4
Generalize the Principle
Formulate the rule: wujub attaches to the cause (sabab) and persists unless the person becomes permanently incapable of the act's ruling. Address and burden only matter for performance, not for the existence of obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و بأسباب وضعت للأحكام، إذا لم يَخلُ الوجوب عن حكمه، وليس في الوجوب تكليف وخطاب، وإنما ذلك في الأداء. ولا خطاب ولا تكليف على الصبي بمجرد العقل حتى يبلغ، فثبت أنه غير مخاطب بالإيمان، لكن صحة الأداء تُبتنى على كون الشيء مشروعاً، وعلى قدرة الأداء، لا على الخطاب ،والتكليف كالمسافر يؤدي الجمعة من غير خطاب ولا تكليف. والإغماء لما لم يناف حكم وجوب الصوم: لم يناف وجوبه، وكان منافياً لحكم وجوب الصلاة إذا امتد، فكان منافياً لوجوبه. والنومُ لمَّا لم يكن منافياً لحكم الوجوب إذا انتبه: لم يكن منافياً للوجوب أيضاً، والله أعلم.
And by causes established for rulings, when obligation is not devoid of its ruling, and there is in obligation no taklif or khitab; rather that is in performance. There is no khitab or taklif upon a minor merely by reason until he reaches puberty, so it is established that he is not addressed with iman, but the validity of performance is based on the act being legislated and on the capacity to perform, not on khitab and taklif, like a traveler performing Friday prayer without khitab or taklif. Unconsciousness, since it does not contradict the ruling of the obligation of fasting, does not contradict its obligation, but it contradicts the ruling of the obligation of prayer if it extends, so it contradicts its obligation. And sleep, since it does not contradict the ruling of obligation when one wakes up, does not contradict obligation either. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 715

Commentary
This passage is a legal rule regarding the nature of obligation (wujub) and its distinction from address (khitab) and burden (taklif). The author establishes that wujub itself is not equivalent to being addressed; rather, address and burden pertain to performance (ada'). A minor is not addressed with iman (faith) simply by possessing reason until puberty, but if he performs iman sincerely, it is valid because validity of performance depends on the act being legislated (mashru') and the capacity to perform (qudrat al-ada), not on being formally addressed. The author draws an analogy with a traveler: he is not addressed with Friday prayer (since it is not obligatory on him), but if he performs it, it is valid. Then the author discusses states that affect obligation: unconsciousness (ighma') does not negate the obligation of fasting (since it does not negate the ruling of obligation if one recovers), but if it extends, it negates the obligation of prayer because the ruling of prayer's obligation requires consciousness. Sleep does not negate obligation because when one wakes, the ruling remains. This is a foundational rule in Hanafi usul: wujub is a constant ruling attached to the cause (sabab) and does not depend on the person being aware of it.

Key Terms
الوجوب (al-wujub): The legal quality of an act being obligatory, which exists even without an address (khitab).
الأداء (al-ada'): The actual performance of an act of worship or legal obligation.
الخطاب (al-khitab): Divine address or command directed at the mukallaf.
التكليف (al-taklif): The burden of legal obligation that requires the person to be capable of understanding the address.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the effect of sleep on the obligation of prayer?
A) Sleep negates the obligation.
B) Sleep does not negate the obligation because when one wakes, the ruling remains.
C) Sleep only negates the obligation if it occurs during the time.
D) Sleep makes the prayer invalid.

Key Takeaway
Obligation (wujub) is attached to the cause and persists independently of address or burden; only performance requires those.

Types of Capacity for Execution (أهلية الأداء) and Their Basis
Definition and categorization of capacity for execution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between restricted and complete capacity for execution, explain how each is established, and state the role of puberty in Sharia.

Core Idea
Capacity for execution is either restricted (deficient reason) or complete; puberty is the Sharia's proxy for balanced reason.

In this passage, Imam al-Bazdawi introduces the two categories of legal capacity to perform acts. Understanding this distinction is fundamental for knowing when a person's actions carry legal consequences and when they are free from liability. Let's explore how the Sharia defines these categories and the evidentiary basis for them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of capacity
Read the first sentence: 'أهلية الأداء نوعان: قاصر، وكامل.' Recognize that restricted (قاصر) applies to those with deficient reason (child, insane), and complete (كامل) to those with sound reason, typically after puberty.
The term 'قاصر' literally means 'falling short'.
2
Understand how restricted capacity is established
The text says restricted capacity is established by bodily ability when deficient, before puberty, and also after puberty for the insane. Note that the insane person has some reason but it is imbalanced.
The foundation of reason is known by a person's ability to choose beneficial acts while considering hidden consequences (عواقب مستورة). This is a rational proof (dalil aqli).
3
Learn the Sharia's proxy for balance of reason
Since balance of reason varies among people, the Sharia sets puberty as the equivalent of balance. Once a person reaches puberty, they are considered to have complete capacity for execution.
Puberty is a legal marker; it does not mean every post-pubescent has perfect reason, but the law treats them as such.
4
Apply: classify a child before puberty and an insane adult
Both have restricted capacity. Their acts are subject to special rulings discussed in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب
أهلية الأداء
وأما أهلية الأداء فنوعان : قاصر، وكامل.
أما القاصر فيثبت بقدرة البدن إذا كانت قاصرةً قبل البلوغ، وكذلك بعد البلوغ فيمن كان معتوهاً؛ لأنه بمنزلة الصبي؛ لأنه عاقل لم يعتدل عقله.
وأصل العقل يُعرف بدلالة العيان، وذلك أن يختار المرء ما يصلح له بدَرْك العواقب المستورة فيما يأتيه ويَذَرُه، وكذلك القصور يُعرف بالامتحان.
فأما الاعتدال : فأمر يتفاوت فيه البشر ، فإذا ترقى عن رتبة القصور: أُقيم البلوغ مقامَ الاعتدال في أحكام الشرع، والأحكام في هذا الباب منقسمة على ما مر.
فأما حقوق الله تعالى، فمنها ما هو حسن لا يحتمل غيره، ولا عهدةَ فيه بوجه، وهو الإيمان بالله تعالى، فوجب القول بصحته من الصبي لما ثبتت أهلية أدائه ، ووجد منه بحقيقته ؛ لأن الشيء إذا وجد بحقيقته : لم ينعدم إلا بحَجْرٍ من الشرع، وذلك في الإيمان باطل؛ لما قلنا إنه حسن لا يحتمل غيره، ولا عهداً فيه إلا في لزوم أدائه، وذلك يحتمل الوضع عنه، فأما الأداء فخال عن العهدة ؛ لأن حرمان الإرث يضاف إلى كفر الباقي، وكذلك الفرقة، ولأن ما يلزمه بعد الإيمان فمن ثمراته. وإنما تتعرف صحة الشيء من حكمه الذي وضع له، وهو سعادة الآخرة، لا من ثمراته ألا يُرى أنها تلزمه إذا ثبت له حكم الإيمان تبعاً لغيره، ولم يُعد عهدة.
ومنها ما هو قبيح لا يحتمل غيره، وهو الجهل بالصانع، والكفر به، ألا يُرى أنه لا يُرَدُّ علمه بوالديه فكيف يُرَدُّ علمه بالله تعالى؟! وكذلك الجهل بغير الله تعالى لا يُعدُّ منه علماً، فكيف الجهل بالله تعالى؟!
وإذا كان كذلك : لم يصلح أن تُجعل ردَّتُه عفواً، بل كان صحيحاً في أحكام الآخرة، وما يلزمه من أحكام الدنيا بالردة: فإنما يلزمه حكماً لصحته، لا قصداً إليه، فلم يصلح العفو عن مثله ، كما إذا ثبت تبعاً.
ومن ذلك : ما هو بين هذين القسمين فقلنا فيه بصحة الأداء من غير عهدة، حتى قلنا بسقوط الوجوب في الكل ؛ لأن اللزوم لا يخلو عن العهدة، وقد شرعت بدون ذلك الوصف، وقلنا بصحتها تطوعاً بلا لزوم مضي، ولا وجوب قضاء؛ لأنها قد شرعت كذلك.
ألا يُرى أن البالغ إذا شَرع فيها على ظنّ أنها عليه وليست عليه: أن اللزوم يبطل عنه.
وكذلك إذا شرع في الإحرام على هذا الوجه، ثم أُحصر: فلا قضاء عليه، فقلنا في الصبي إذا أحرم صح منه بلا عهدة، حتى إذا ارتكب محظوراً لم يلزمه شيء.
Chapter of Capacity for Execution. As for capacity for execution, it is of two types: restricted and complete. As for restricted, it is established by bodily ability when it is deficient before puberty, and similarly after puberty for one who is insane because he is like a child; he is rational but his reason is not balanced. The foundation of reason is known by direct evidence, namely that a person chooses what is beneficial for him by perceiving hidden consequences in what he does and refrains from. Similarly, deficiency is known by examination. As for balance, it is a matter that varies among humans. When it rises above the level of deficiency, puberty is made the equivalent of balance in the rulings of Sharia. The rulings in this chapter are divided as mentioned. As for the rights of Allah Almighty, among them is what is good and admits no alternative, and there is no liability in it at all, and that is faith in Allah Almighty. So it is necessary to rule its validity from a child because his capacity for execution is established and it occurred from him in its reality. For if something occurs in its reality, it is not annulled except by a prohibition from the Sharia. That is invalid in faith because we said it is good and admits no alternative, and there is no covenant except in the obligation of its performance, and that can be waived; as for performance, it is free from liability. Because deprivation of inheritance is attributed to the disbelief of the remaining [heirs], and similarly separation, and because what becomes obligatory after faith is from its fruits. The validity of a thing is known by its ruling for which it was legislated, which is happiness in the hereafter, not from its fruits. Do you not see that it becomes binding on him when the ruling of faith is established for him as a consequence of others, and liability is not counted? Among them is what is evil and admits no alternative, which is ignorance of the Creator and disbelief in Him. Do you not see that his knowledge of his parents is not rejected, so how can his knowledge of Allah Almighty be rejected? Similarly, ignorance of other than Allah Almighty is not considered knowledge from him, so how about ignorance of Allah Almighty? Since this is so, it is not proper to make his apostasy forgiven; rather, it is valid in the rulings of the hereafter. And what becomes binding on him from the worldly rulings due to apostasy, it becomes binding as a ruling due to its validity, not as an intention towards it. So forgiveness for such is not proper, just as when it is established as a consequence. Among that is what is between these two categories. So we said regarding it the validity of execution without liability, to the extent that we said the obligation drops completely because binding does not lack liability, and it was legislated without that description. We said its validity as a supererogatory act without binding performance and without obligation of makeup, because it was legislated thus. Do you not see that if an adult begins [an act] thinking it is obligatory upon him while it is not, the binding is nullified for him. Similarly, if he begins ihram in this manner, then is prevented, there is no makeup upon him. So we said regarding a child, if he assumes ihram, it is valid from him without liability, such that if he commits a prohibited act, nothing is incumbent upon him.
Source pages p. 716

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Imam al-Bazdawi on capacity for execution (أهلية الأداء). It begins by defining two types: restricted and complete. Restricted capacity pertains to those before puberty and the insane, whose bodily ability is present but reasoning is incomplete. The author then explains that the validity of acts from such persons depends on the nature of the act itself. Acts that are purely good (like faith) are valid because they admit no alternative and bring no liability. Acts that are purely evil (like disbelief) are also considered valid and entail consequences because they cannot be ignored. Acts that fall in between (like prayer or fasting) are valid from a child but without binding obligation or liability; he may perform them as supererogatory. The example of ihram illustrates: a child's ihram is valid, but if he violates a prohibition, no penalty is due because there is no liability. This nuanced approach reflects the Hanafi understanding that capacity is established for these categories based on the intrinsic nature of the act, not merely on the person's legal status.

Key Terms
أهلية الأداء (ahlīyat al-adā'): Capacity for execution; the legal competency to perform acts that have legal effects, divided into restricted (قاصر) and complete (كامل).
قاصر (qāṣir): Restricted capacity; a person whose bodily ability is present but cognitive reasoning is deficient, such as a child before puberty or an insane person.
عهدة (ʿuhda): Liability or responsibility for an act; in this context, the legal obligation to fulfill or be accountable for an act, including penalty for violations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the evidentiary basis for knowing the foundation of reason (أصل العقل)?
A) Direct revelation from the Quran
B) A person's ability to choose beneficial acts by perceiving hidden consequences
C) The consensus of scholars
D) The attainment of puberty

Key Takeaway
Capacity for execution is never absent; it is either restricted (with deficient reasoning) or complete, and the Sharia uses bodily maturity as the marker for complete capacity.
